Questions on the Old and New Testament

Text from OpenGreekAndLatin/csel-dev (A. Souter, ed., Pseudo-Augustini Quaestiones Veteris et Novi Testamenti CXXVII, CSEL 50, Vienna 1908 — public domain text; TEI encoding CC BY-SA 4.0).

Table of Contents

  • Book of Questions [of Saint Augustine] on the Old and New Testament, Questions to the Number of 127
  • I. WHAT IS GOD?
  • II. WHY GOD MADE THE WORLD.
  • III. WHAT NEED WAS THERE TO SET FORTH THROUGH MOSES, AND NOT BEFORE, THE BEGINNING OF THE WORLD AND THE ORDER OF CREATION?
  • IIII. WHY DID HE NOT GIVE THE LAW AT THE VERY BEGINNING?
  • V. FOR WHAT REASON WAS ABEL'S SACRIFICE ACCEPTED AND CAIN'S REJECTED?
  • VI. WHETHER LAMECH KILLED CAIN, AS IS SUPPOSED?
  • VII. WHAT TEN WORDS WERE GIVEN ON THE TABLETS, OR HOW MANY WORDS APIECE DID THE INDIVIDUAL TABLETS HAVE?
  • VIII. WHY DID MOSES, COMING DOWN FROM THE MOUNTAIN WITH THE TABLETS, HAVE A COUNTENANCE SPLENDID AND UNBEARABLE?
  • VIIII. IF GOD MADE ALL THINGS GOOD, AND VERY GOOD, HOW IS IT THAT HE SAYS TO NOAH, 'OF THE CLEAN AND THE UNCLEAN BRING WITH YOU INTO THE ARK,' SINCE, ABSOLUTELY SPEAKING, THE UNCLEAN CANNOT BE CALLED GOOD?
  • X. SINCE GOD SAYS TO ABRAHAM CONCERNING THE SONS OF ISRAEL THAT THEY WOULD GO OUT FROM THE POWER OF THE EGYPTIANS IN THE FOURTH GENERATION, HOW IS IT THAT, ON THE CONTRARY, THE LAW SAYS: 'IN THE FIFTH GENERATION THE SONS OF ISRAEL WENT OUT FROM THE LAND OF EGYPT'? IT SEEMS VERY MUCH A CONTRADICTION.
  • XI. IF THE WILL OF A JUST MAN IS GOOD, HOW IS IT THAT ISAAC BLESSED NOT ESAU, WHOM HE WISHED, BUT JACOB, WHOM HE DID NOT WISH?
  • XII. WHY DID ABRAHAM RECEIVE CIRCUMCISION AS THE SIGN OF HIS FAITH?
  • XIII. IF THE JUDGMENT OF GOD IS JUST, WHY WERE THE INFANTS IN SODOM BURNED TOGETHER WITH THEIR PARENTS?
  • XIIII. HOW IS IT THAT GOD, WHO IS PROCLAIMED JUST, PROMISED THAT HE WOULD REPAY THE SINS OF THE FATHERS UPON THE SONS UNTO THE THIRD AND FOURTH GENERATION?
  • XV. SINCE THE LAW PROCLAIMS THE JUST MAN, AND HE IS TRULY JUST WHO HAS FULL JUSTICE, YET, ON THE CONTRARY, SOLOMON SAYS: 'DO NOT BE JUST OVERMUCH.'
  • XVI. WHY WAS THE ANGEL, WHO WISHED TO KILL MOSES ON THE WAY, APPEASED BY THE CIRCUMCISION OF THE INFANT?
  • XVII. HOW IS IT THAT HE CALLS ACCURSED THOSE WHO HAVE NOT LEFT SEED IN ISRAEL, BUT THROUGH ISAIAH HE SAYS THAT IT IS NO HINDRANCE TO EUNUCHS THAT THEY CANNOT BEGET?
  • XVIII. WHY DID SAUL, WHEN HE SINNED, ASK THAT PRAYER BE MADE FOR HIM, THAT HE MIGHT BE FORGIVEN, AND WAS UNABLE TO OBTAIN IT, WHEREAS DAVID, WHEN HE SINNED, MADE HIS REQUEST AND OBTAINED PARDON?
  • XVIIII. IT MUST BE ASKED WHETHER ADAM, WHEN MADE, HAD AN IMMORTAL BODY OR A MORTAL ONE.
  • XX. WHAT DOES IT MEAN WHEN IT SAYS: 'MAN ATE THE BREAD OF ANGELS', SINCE ANGELS HAVE NO NEED OF FOOD, INASMUCH AS THEY ARE SIMPLE IN NATURE AND FLOURISH WITH SPIRITUAL POWER?
  • XXI. WHAT IS IT TO HAVE MADE MAN TO THE IMAGE AND LIKENESS OF GOD, AND WHETHER WOMAN IS THE IMAGE OF GOD.
  • XXII. WHAT DOES IT MEAN THAT SOLOMON SAYS: 'JUSTIFY YOUR SOUL BEFORE YOUR DEATH', AND IN THE PSALM: 'NO LIVING MAN,' HE SAYS, 'SHALL BE JUSTIFIED IN THE SIGHT OF GOD'?
  • XXIII. WHETHER SOULS ARE FROM PROPAGATION LIKE BODIES.
  • XXIIII. HOW IS IT THAT, SINCE MAN AND WOMAN ARE ONE FLESH, THE MAN IS THE IMAGE OF GOD, AND NOT ALSO THE WOMAN?
  • XXV. WHY DOES JOSEPH, AFTER HIS PROPHECY, ADJURE THE SONS OF ISRAEL THAT, WHEN THEY WERE DELIVERED BY GOD, THEY SHOULD CARRY HIS ASHES OUT OF EGYPT?
  • XXVI. IT MUST BE INQUIRED CONCERNING ELISHA WHETHER HE OBTAINED THAT WHICH HE IS SAID TO HAVE ASKED FROM ELIJAH WITH DIFFICULTY.
  • XXVII. WHETHER THE WITCH RAISED UP SAMUEL AND HE HIMSELF WAS SEEN BY HER AND SPOKE TO SAUL, WHICH THE NARRATIVE RELATES IN THE BOOK OF KINGS.
  • XXVIII. WHAT MUST BE OBJECTED AGAINST THOSE WHO SAY THAT THIS WORLD IS MOVED NATURALLY FROM ETERNITY AND IS SUBJECT NEITHER TO A BEGINNING NOR TO AN END.
  • XXVIIII. WHY WAS IT COMMANDED THAT CIRCUMCISION BE PERFORMED ON THE EIGHTH DAY? .
  • XXX. IN PROVERBS: 'THE JUST MAN,' HE SAYS, 'IS HIS OWN ACCUSER AT THE BEGINNING OF HIS SPEECH': HOW IS HE JUST, IF A SINNER?
  • XXXI. WHETHER THE SERPENT SPOKE WITH THE WOMAN BY NATURE, OR WHETHER THE DEVIL, CALLED A SERPENT BY HIS DEED, SEDUCED HER.
  • XXXII. WE READ IN SOLOMON: 'THE RICH AND THE POOR MET ONE ANOTHER; BUT GOD MADE THEM BOTH': HOW THEN IS THERE NO RESPECT OF PERSONS WITH GOD?
  • XXXIII. SOLOMON: 'THE YEARS,' HE SAYS, 'OF THE WICKED SHALL BE SHORTENED.' WHEREAS WE SEE SOME OF THE WICKED LONG-LIVED.
  • XXXIIII. IN SOLOMON: 'GOD,' HE SAYS, 'DID NOT MAKE DEATH', AND IN ANOTHER PLACE: 'GOOD AND EVIL, LIFE AND DEATH, POVERTY AND HONOR ARE FROM GOD'.
  • XXXV. FOR WHAT REASON DOES DAVID CALL SAUL, AFTER GOD HAD DEPARTED FROM HIM, THE LORD'S ANOINTED, AND SHOW HIM DEFERENCE?
  • XXXVI. IF 'THE SOUL THAT SINS SHALL ITSELF DIE', HOW IS IT THAT ACHAN THE SON OF CARMI SINNED AND THIRTY-SIX MEN WERE SLAIN ON HIS ACCOUNT?
  • XXXVII. HOW IS IT THAT THE DEATH SENT UPON JACOB CAME UPON ISRAEL, SINCE JACOB HIMSELF WAS CALLED ISRAEL?
  • XXXVIII. IF THE HORSE AND THE MULE HAVE NO UNDERSTANDING, HOW MUCH MORE THE EARTH, A THING WITHOUT SENSE? HOW IS IT THEN THAT THE EARTH IS SAID TO BLESS GOD?
  • XXXVIIII. WHAT IS IT THAT IS READ IN SOLOMON: 'THERE IS HOPE,' HE SAYS, 'IN THE DARKNESS; A LIVING DOG IS BETTER THAN A DEAD LION'?
  • XL. What does the prophet mean when he says: 'Rejoice, O barren one who does not bear; break forth and cry aloud, you who are not in travail, for the children of the forsaken one are more than of her who has a husband'?
  • XLI. Whether the Spirit who was borne over the waters is to be understood as the Holy Spirit, since it is said: 'The Spirit of God was borne over the water.'
  • XLII. Why did the angel sent to speak to Moses appear in fire and in a bush on the mountain?
  • XLIII. Since we know that Abraham was forbidden by God to sacrifice his son, why was Jephthah not forbidden when he offered up his daughter, but discharged his vow to God with human blood?
  • XLIV. Against the Jews.
  • XLV. On the image.
  • XLVI. On Samuel.
  • XLVII. On the reading of the prophet Isaiah: 'And seven women shall take hold of one man, saying: We will eat our own bread and be covered with our own garments; only let your name be invoked upon us. Take away our reproach.'
  • XLVIII. God is surely perfection and in need of nothing: what need then was there of Christ the Savior, that he should be born of God and that God should have a Son through whom he might make all things?
  • XLIX. Why was the Savior baptized, since he was born holy and was called Christ the Lord at his very birth, given that baptism is for the sake of purification and of sin?
  • L. If the Savior was baptized in order to be an example, why, having been circumcised, did he forbid the rest to be circumcised?
  • LI. How is it to be understood that, when Mary said to the angel: 'And how shall I know this, since I have not known a man?', the angel Gabriel answered: 'The Holy Spirit shall come upon you, and the power of the Most High shall overshadow you.'
  • LII. If Christ was born of the Holy Spirit, that is, made flesh from Mary by his working, why is it said: 'Wisdom' — which surely is Christ — 'has built herself a house'?
  • LIII. If all things were done for a reason, why is the Savior said to have been born on the eighth day before the Kalends of January?
  • LIV. If Christ was made a son to God from the seed of David according to the flesh — that is, being now born, he is the Son of God in both respects, since he was born holy — how then, after he was baptized, was it said to him by the Lord God: 'You are my Son, this day I have begotten you'?
  • LV. What was the reason that the Lord allowed himself to be given over to the cross at that time when the Jews kept the Passover on the eighth day before the Kalends of April?
  • LVI. Why is Joseph's father written as Jacob in Matthew and as Heli in Luke, so that either he is unskillfully described as having two fathers or at least it is not known who his true father is?
  • LVII. HOW IS IT THAT, ALTHOUGH IT IS WRITTEN IN THE PROPHET MALACHI: 'BEHOLD, I SEND MY ANGEL BEFORE THY FACE, WHO SHALL PREPARE THY WAY', THE EVANGELIST MARK ASSERTS THAT THIS WAS WRITTEN IN THE PROPHET ISAIAH?
  • LVIII. FOR WHAT REASON DOES JOHN DENY THAT HE KNEW CHRIST BEFORE THE BAPTISM, WHEN, AS HE COMES TO HIM FOR BAPTISM, HE SAYS TO HIM: 'I OUGHT TO BE BAPTIZED BY THEE, AND COMEST THOU TO ME?' HOW DID HE NOT KNOW HIM WHOM HE FORBADE, HUMBLING HIMSELF BEFORE HIM?
  • LVIIII. IF BAPTISM IS A HEAVENLY MYSTERY, WHY, WHEN THE LORD SPEAKS TO NICODEMUS AS HE DOUBTS CONCERNING BAPTISM, DOES HE SAY: 'IF I HAVE TOLD YOU EARTHLY THINGS AND YE BELIEVE NOT, HOW, IF I SHALL TELL YOU HEAVENLY THINGS, WILL YE BELIEVE?'
  • LX. IF 'THE LAW AND THE PROPHETS WERE UNTIL JOHN', HOW DOES THE SAVIOUR SEND TO THE PRIESTS THAT GIFTS BE OFFERED FOR THE CLEANSING OF LEPROSY?
  • LXI. HOW IS IT THAT, WHEN THE JEWS ACCUSED THE DISCIPLES OF VIOLATING THE SABBATH BY RUBBING EARS OF CORN WITH THEIR HANDS AND EATING THEM, THE SAVIOUR BROUGHT FORWARD THE EXAMPLE OF DAVID, BECAUSE HE ATE THE LOAVES WHICH IT WAS NOT LAWFUL FOR HIM TO EAT BUT FOR THE PRIESTS ALONE, BY WHICH THEY DO NOT SEEM TO BE EXCUSED, BUT RATHER TO BE MADE GUILTY TOGETHER WITH DAVID, SEEING THAT DAVID DID NOT EVEN DO THIS ON THE SABBATH?
  • LXII. HOW IS IT THAT, WHEN THE SONS OF LEAH, WHO WERE OF THE TRIBE OF JUDAH, WERE SLAIN, RACHEL IS SAID TO BEWAIL HER OWN SONS?
  • LXIII. FOR WHAT REASON DID THE CHALDEAN MAGI, THROUGH THE APPEARANCE OF A STAR, UNDERSTAND THAT CHRIST THE KING OF THE JEWS WAS BORN, WHEN BY A STAR AS A SIGN A KING IS WONT TO BE MARKED OUT FOR THE TIMES?
  • LXIIII. HOW IS IT PROVED THAT THE SAVIOUR ROSE FROM THE DEAD AFTER THREE DAYS AND NIGHTS?
  • LXV. IF THE EVANGELISTS SPOKE WITH ONE MOUTH AND ONE REASONING, HOW DID IT COME ABOUT THAT, WHEREAS THREE SAY, THAT IS, MATTHEW, LUKE, AND JOHN, THAT THE LORD WAS CRUCIFIED AT THE SIXTH HOUR, MARK ON THE CONTRARY SAYS THAT THE SAVIOUR WAS CRUCIFIED AT THE THIRD HOUR?
  • LXVI. THE EVANGELIST MARK SAYS THAT THE DEMONS KNEW AND CONFESSED JESUS, BUT ON THE CONTRARY THE APOSTLE DENIES THAT THE PRINCES AND POWERS OF THIS WORLD KNEW THE DIVINITY OF THE LORD JESUS. FOR MARK SAYS AMONG OTHER THINGS: 'FOR THEY KNEW THAT IT WAS HE HIMSELF'; BUT THE APOSTLE SAYS: 'WHOM NONE OF THE PRINCES OF THIS WORLD KNEW; FOR HAD THEY KNOWN IT, THEY WOULD NEVER HAVE CRUCIFIED THE LORD OF MAJESTY.' IF THE DEMONS KNEW, HOW DID THE PRINCES NOT KNOW?
  • LXVII. HOW IS IT THAT THE SAVIOUR, PLACED UPON THE CROSS, SAYS: 'FATHER, FORGIVE THEM; FOR THEY KNOW NOT WHAT THEY DO'? IF THEY KNOW NOT, WHAT IS IT THAT IS FORGIVEN, ESPECIALLY WHEN KING ABIMELECH SAYS TO GOD: 'WILT THOU DESTROY A NATION THAT IS IGNORANT?'
  • LXVIII. THE LORD ASSUREDLY TAUGHT THAT WE MUST PRAY FOR OUR ENEMIES: HOW IS IT THAT, ON THE CONTRARY, THE SOULS OF THE SLAIN ASK TO AVENGE THEMSELVES, DEMANDING VENGEANCE FROM GOD?
  • LXVIIII. IF THE LAW CEASED ALREADY WHEN JOHN OR THE SAVIOR WAS PREACHING, HOW DOES THE SAVIOR SAY: 'I HAVE NOT COME TO ABOLISH THE LAW OR THE PROPHETS, BUT TO FULFILL'? FOR IF IT WAS FORBIDDEN, HOW WAS IT NOT ABOLISHED, SEEING THAT IT LOST THE AUTHORITY OF BEING PRACTICED?
  • LXX. THE LORD HAS CERTAINLY COMMANDED THAT WE BECOME ENEMIES TO THE DEVIL; HOW THEN IS IT THAT IN THE GOSPEL HE SAYS: 'BE QUICKLY IN AGREEMENT WITH YOUR ADVERSARY'? WHO IS MAN'S ADVERSARY IF NOT THE DEVIL?
  • LXXI. JACOB WAS CALLED A MAN SEEING GOD, AND MOSES SAW GOD FACE TO FACE, AND SO ALSO DID ISAIAH: 'I HAVE SEEN,' HE SAYS, 'THE GOD OF SABAOTH WITH MY OWN EYES'; BUT ON THE CONTRARY JOHN THE EVANGELIST: 'NO ONE,' HE SAYS, 'HAS EVER SEEN GOD.' THIS, AS FAR AS IT SEEMS, IS CONTRADICTORY.
  • LXXII. (LXXVI). IN THE GOSPEL JOHN SAYS: 'THE LAW WAS GIVEN THROUGH MOSES, BUT GRACE AND TRUTH CAME THROUGH JESUS CHRIST'; THEREFORE BEFORE THIS IT DID NOT EXIST. HOW THEN SHALL THE LAW BE SAID TO HAVE BEEN GIVEN BY GOD, IN WHICH THERE WAS NO TRUTH?
  • LXXIII. (LXXVII). WHAT IS THE MEANING OF WHAT MARK THE EVANGELIST SAYS AMONG OTHER THINGS ABOUT CHRIST: 'ENTERING,' HE SAYS, 'INTO THE HOUSE HE WISHED NO ONE TO KNOW IT, AND HE COULD NOT BE HIDDEN'? IF THEREFORE HE WISHED IT AND COULD NOT, HIS WILL SEEMS TO HAVE BEEN WEAKENED.
  • LXXIIII. (LXXVIII). IT IS READ IN THE GOSPEL OF JOHN THAT, ALTHOUGH THE SAVIOR HAD DENIED THAT HE WOULD GO UP TO THE FEAST DAY, HE WENT UP. THIS SEEMS TO BELONG TO AN INCONSISTENT PERSON.
  • LXXV. (LXXIX). IF WE LIVE BY OUR OWN JUDGMENT, WHY DID THE SAVIOR SAY: 'NO ONE COMES,' HE SAYS, 'TO ME, UNLESS THE FATHER WHO SENT ME HAS DRAWN HIM,' AND, IN AGREEMENT WITH THESE WORDS, THE APOSTLE: 'IT IS NOT OF HIM WHO WILLS,' HE SAYS, 'NOR OF HIM WHO RUNS, BUT OF GOD WHO SHOWS MERCY,' AND: 'ON WHOM HE WILLS HE HAS MERCY, AND WHOM HE WILLS HE HARDENS'? HOW IS THE JUDGMENT OF THE WILL FREE, WHEN BY ANOTHER'S BIDDING IT IS LED EITHER TO GOOD OR TO EVIL?
  • LXXVI. (LXXII). IT IS READ IN THE APOCALYPSE OF JOHN: 'GO,' HE SAYS, (AND TAKE THE BOOK FROM THE HAND OF THE ANGEL AND DEVOUR IT, AND IT WILL MAKE YOUR BELLY BITTER, BUT IN YOUR MOUTH IT WILL BE SWEET AS HONEY). WHAT IS THIS BOOK, WHICH MAKES THE BELLY BITTER, THOUGH IT IS SWEET?
  • LXXVII. (LXXIII). WHAT IS THE MEANING OF WHAT SIMEON SAYS TO MARY THE MOTHER OF THE LORD AMONG OTHER THINGS: 'THIS ONE,' HE SAYS, 'IS SET FOR THE FALL AND RISING AGAIN OF MANY IN ISRAEL; AND A SWORD SHALL PIERCE THROUGH YOUR OWN SOUL, THAT THE THOUGHTS OF MANY HEARTS MAY BE REVEALED'?
  • LXXVIII. (LXXIV). WHAT DOES THE PROPHET ISAIAH MEAN WHEN HE SAYS ABOUT CHRIST: 'WHO DID NO SIN'? BUT ON THE CONTRARY THE APOSTLE: 'HIM WHO KNEW NO SIN,' HE SAYS, 'HE MADE TO BE SIN FOR US'?
  • LXXVIIII. (LXXV). WHY DID THE SAVIOR PAY THE DIDRACHMA ONLY FOR HIMSELF AND PETER, AND NOT ALSO FOR THE REST OF THE APOSTLES, SEEING THAT ALL OF THEM FOLLOWED HIM, HAVING LEFT ALL THAT WAS THEIRS?
  • LXXX. CERTAINLY ONE IS EITHER A SON OF GOD OR OF THE DEVIL: THEREFORE ONE IS ALWAYS A SON, BUT SOMETIMES OF GOD, SOMETIMES OF THE DEVIL. IT MUST THEREFORE BE INQUIRED WHAT WE ARE WHEN WE ARE BORN.
  • LXXXI. THE APOSTLE SAYS: "WE ARE JEWS BY NATURE." HE THEREFORE SHOWS THAT JEWS ARE BORN FROM JEWS — I DO NOT SPEAK OF PROSELYTES, WHO, IT IS AGREED, ARE MADE JEWS. FINALLY, THOSE WHO WERE BORN IN THE DESERT WERE NOT CIRCUMCISED —: IF THEREFORE JEWS ARE BORN FROM JEWS, WHY NOT ALSO CHRISTIANS FROM CHRISTIANS? FOR PAGANS TOO ARE BORN FROM PAGANS.
  • LXXXII. THAT THE PAGANS ARE SUBJECT TO THE ELEMENTS NO ONE DOUBTS: WHAT THEN IS IT THAT THE APOSTLE SAYS: 'WE TOO WERE SERVING UNDER THE ELEMENTS OF THIS WORLD'? IF THEREFORE THE JEWS TOO WERE SERVING THE ELEMENTS, HOW DID THEY DIFFER FROM THE PAGANS?
  • LXXXIII. IF THROUGH CHRIST THERE IS SALVATION AND TRUE AND PERFECT KNOWLEDGE, WHY DID IT NOT COME EARLIER, SO THAT OUR PREDECESSORS ALSO, WHO WERE IN IGNORANCE, MIGHT LEARN THE TRUTH? FINALLY, AFTER THE COMING OF CHRIST MANY MORE HAVE BEEN SAVED THAN BEFORE. WHENCE, IF HE HAD COME EARLIER, MANY MORE WOULD HAVE BEEN SAVED. IF THEREFORE IT IS SO, IT SEEMS REPREHENSIBLE.
  • LXXXIIII. WHY, WHILE WE REPREHEND THE PAGANS FOR OBSERVING THE COURSE OF THE MOON IN THE RECKONING OF EASTER, DO WE OBSERVE THE LUNAR DAYS AND THE MEASURE?
  • LXXXV. WHAT IS IT THAT, ALTHOUGH IT IS AGREED THAT FROM DAVID DOWN TO THE TRANSMIGRATION OF BABYLON THERE ARE SEVENTEEN GENERATIONS, THE EVANGELIST SAYS FOURTEEN, OCHOZIAS BEING PASSED OVER, WHO IS AFTER JORAM THE SON OF JEHOSHAPHAT, AND JOASH THE SON OF OCHOZIAS, AND AMASIAS THE SON OF JOASH?
  • LXXXVI. WHAT IS IT THAT PROVES THAT MARY THE MOTHER OF THE LORD IS OF THE TRIBE AND SEED OF DAVID?
  • LXXXVII. IF GOD IS ONE, WHY IS THE HOPE OF SALVATION IN THREE, AND NOT IN TWO OR FOUR OR INDEED IN THE ONE HIMSELF? AND WHY WAS THE TRINITY NOT PROCLAIMED FROM THE BEGINNING?
  • LXXXVIII. IF GREATER GRACE AND CLEARER UNDERSTANDING IS IN THE NEW THAN IN THE OLD, WHY DID ISAIAH THE PROPHET SEE THE LORD SABAOTH, WHO IS CHRIST, SITTING ON THE THRONE OF MAJESTY, ACCORDING TO THE INTERPRETATION OF JOHN THE EVANGELIST — FOR HE SAID AMONG OTHER THINGS: 'THESE THINGS ISAIAH SAID, WHEN HE SAW HIS MAJESTY AND SPOKE OF HIM' —, BUT IN THE NEW STEPHEN THE FIRST MARTYR SAYS THAT HE SAW JESUS STANDING AT THE RIGHT HAND OF GOD? WHAT IS THIS, THAT HERE HE SEEMS AS IF SUBJECTED AFTER HIS TRIUMPHS, AND THERE AS IF LORD, BEFORE HE HAD CONQUERED?
  • LXXXVIIII.
  • XC. IF THE DEVIL HIMSELF IS SATAN, WHAT IS IT THAT AMONG OTHER THINGS THE SAVIOR SAYS TO THE JEWS: 'YOU ARE OF YOUR FATHER THE DEVIL, AND YOU WISH TO DO THE DESIRES OF YOUR FATHER. HE WAS A MURDERER FROM THE BEGINNING AND DID NOT STAND IN THE TRUTH, BECAUSE TRUTH IS NOT IN HIM. WHEN HE SPEAKS A LIE, HE SPEAKS FROM HIS OWN, BECAUSE HE IS A LIAR, AS IS HIS FATHER ALSO'?
  • XCI. IT MUST BE INQUIRED IN WHAT WAY PHOTINUS IS TO BE CONTRADICTED, WITHOUT ARGUMENTS, THAT CHRIST EXISTED BEFORE MARY.
  • XCII. IN WHAT WAY IS IT UNDERSTOOD WHAT THE SAVIOR SAYS: 'PEACE I GIVE TO YOU, MY PEACE I LEAVE TO YOU; NOT AS THIS WORLD GIVES, DO I GIVE TO YOU'?
  • XCIII. It must be asked whether the apostles had the Holy Spirit at that time when they were with the Lord, since among many things the Evangelist says: 'The Spirit,' he says, 'had not yet been given, because Jesus had not yet been glorified,' and in another place: 'If you love me,' he says, 'keep my commandments, and I will ask the Father, and he will give you another Paraclete, that he may be with you forever, the Spirit of truth, whom the world cannot receive, because it neither sees nor knows him; you see him and know him, because he abides with you and is with you.' What is this? He denies that the Spirit was given before the passion, yet he promises that he himself will ask the Father to send him. Likewise he adds that he was with them and abode among them; but after the resurrection he is recorded to have breathed upon them and said to them: 'Receive the Holy Spirit,' while at Pentecost the Holy Spirit is recorded to have descended upon the apostles. I see such great confusions in this matter that I do not know what ought to be held.
  • XCIIII. It must be asked whether Judas Iscariot, the betrayer of the Lord, ended his life by the noose before the passion of the Savior.
  • XCV. Whence the observance of Pentecost arose, or for what reason.
  • XCVI. It must be asked whether Pascha is to be interpreted as 'passage,' as it seems to the Greeks.
  • XCVII. By what reasoning the impiety of Arius may be answered simply from the Law.
  • XCVIII. On the Gospel of John.
  • XCVIIII. What is meant by 'Let no temptation take hold of you but such as is human.'
  • C. On the Gospel of Matthew.
  • CI. On the boasting of the Roman Levites.
  • CII. Against Novatian.
  • CIII. Since it is established that in Leviticus the Lord commanded concerning the sacrifices to be offered, how is it that, in his anger, he says to the people that he did not command their fathers to offer libations or sacrifices or holocausts? Finally he speaks thus through the prophet Jeremiah: 'Thus says the Lord: Gather your holocausts together with your sacrifices and eat the flesh, for I did not speak to your fathers nor command them, on the day when I led them out of the land of Egypt, concerning holocausts and sacrifices.'
  • CIIII. On the Gospel of Luke.
  • CV. That the Gospel agrees with prophecy.
  • CVI. On the Book of Genesis.
  • CVII. On the order of day and night.
  • CVIII. On the Hebrew language, from what it received its name.
  • CVIIII. On Melchizedek.
  • CX. On the First Psalm.
  • CXI. On Psalm XXIII.
  • CXII. On Psalm L.
  • CXIII. Why the Son of God was sent and not another.
  • CXIIII. Against the Pagans.
  • CXV. On Fate.
  • CXVI. THE RATIONALE OF THE PASSOVER.
  • CXVII. ON ABRAHAM.
  • CXVIII. ON JOB.
  • CXVIIII. ON TOBIAS.
  • CXX. ON FASTING.
  • CXXI. THE PRAISE AND GLORY OF THE PASSOVER.
  • CXXII. ON THE BEGINNING.
  • CXXIII. WHETHER ADAM HAD THE HOLY SPIRIT?
  • CXXIIII. THAT ONE AND THE SAME DEED DIFFERS ACCORDING TO PERSONS, WHETHER UNTO PRAISE OR UNTO CONDEMNATION.
  • CXXV. AGAINST EUSEBIUS.
  • CXXVI. ON HIM WHO RECEIVES.
  • CXXVII. ON THE SIN OF ADAM AND EVE.
  • QUESTIONS [OF SAINT AUGUSTINE] ON THE OLD AND NEW TESTAMENT.
  • I.
  • II. AGAINST THOSE WHO DENY THAT ANYTHING PERTAINS TO GOD.
  • III.
  • XIII.
  • XIIII.
  • XXXVII. WHY GOD SAID: 'MY SPIRIT SHALL NOT REMAIN IN THESE MEN, BECAUSE THEY ARE FLESH, AND THEIR YEARS SHALL BE A HUNDRED AND TWENTY'?
  • XXXVIII. WHAT THE BLESSING OF JACOB, WHICH HE GAVE, CONTAINS.
  • XXXVIIII.
  • XL. WAS THERE NO OTHER SIGN THAT WAS DONE BY MOSES OPENLY BEFORE PHARAOH EXCEPT THE SERPENT?
  • XLI. WHAT IS THE MEANING OF THAT IN THE PSALM: 'MEN,' HE SAYS, <AND BEASTS THOU WILT SAVE', AND TO THE PROPHET JONAH: 'I WILL NOT SPARE,' HE SAYS, 'THE CITY IN WHICH DWELL 120,000 MEN AND MUCH CATTLE', BUT ON THE CONTRARY THE APOSTLE: 'IS IT,' HE SAYS, 'THAT GOD HAS CARE FOR OXEN?'
  • XLII. IF ADAM, MADE BY GOD AND ENSOULED, RECEIVED THE HOLY SPIRIT, BECAUSE IT IS WRITTEN: 'GOD BREATHED INTO HIS FACE THE SPIRIT OF LIFE'?
  • XLIII.
  • XLIIII.
  • XLV. 'IN THE SUN', HE SAYS, 'HE SET HIS TABERNACLE,' THAT IS, HIS BODY, IN WHICH CHRIST DWELT, BECAUSE HE WAS BEATEN WITH SCOURGES BY PILATE: HOW THEN IN THE PSALM CONCERNING CHRIST: 'THE SCOURGE SHALL NOT COME NEAR THY TABERNACLE', SEEING THAT HE CALLED HIS BODY A TEMPLE?
  • XLVI. WHY ADAM, PLACED IN THE WORLD, RECEIVED A COMMANDMENT OR LAW, ALTHOUGH HE HIMSELF HELD DOMINION OVER THE REST.
  • XLVII. THE OLD LAW ALLEGES THAT GOD SWORE — FOR THUS IT SAYS: 'BY MY VERY SELF HAVE I SWORN, SAYS THE LORD' —, BUT THE SAVIOR FORBADE SWEARING: HOW DID HE NOT DESTROY THE OLD THINGS?
  • XLVIII. WHY IN THE LAW IT WAS SAID EVEN TO AARON HIMSELF THAT HE SHOULD OFFER HOLOCAUSTS FOR HIS OWN SINS, ALTHOUGH DAVID SAYS: 'FOR OFFENSES THOU HAST NOT REQUIRED A HOLOCAUST' AND IN WHAT FOLLOWS: 'THOU WILT NOT BE DELIGHTED WITH HOLOCAUSTS.' HOW DID HE COMMAND THAT TO BE OFFERED IN WHICH HE IS NOT DELIGHTED?
  • XLVIIII. WHY DID SOLOMON HAVE THE SPIRIT OF WISDOM, WHEN HE DID NOT HAVE A PURE LIFE? FOR HE TOOK GREAT DELIGHT IN WOMEN, AND THROUGH THIS HE SINNED.
  • L. IN TOBIT: 'IT IS AN HONORABLE THING,' HE SAYS, 'TO REVEAL AND CONFESS THE WORKS OF GOD'; BUT THE SAVIOR, WHILE DOING THE WORK OF GOD: 'TELL IT TO NO ONE,' HE SAYS.
  • LI. WHY WERE CIRCUMCISION AND THE COMMANDMENTS GIVEN TO THE PEOPLE, WHICH FORMERLY DID NOT EXIST AND ARE NOT NOW HELD IN AUTHORITY?
  • LII.
  • LIII.
  • LIIII. IN WISDOM: 'HE WHO CREATED,' HE SAYS, 'THE WORLD OUT OF UNFORMED MATTER' AND, ON THE OTHER HAND: 'BECAUSE WE WERE MADE OUT OF NOTHING.'
  • LV.
  • QUESTIONS ON THE NEW TESTAMENT.
  • I.
  • II.
  • III. WHY WERE THE DEEDS AND SAYINGS OF THE LORD ARRANGED INTO SCRIPTURE IN FOUR VOLUMES AND BY FOUR WRITERS?
  • IIII. SINCE IT IS ESTABLISHED THAT FOUR BOOKS OF THE DEEDS AND SAYINGS OF THE LORD WERE DULY COMPOSED, IT MUST BE KNOWN WHAT THEIR ORDER IS.
  • V. WHY, IN DESCRIBING THE GOSPEL OF CHRIST, DOES MATTHEW SAY: 'THE BOOK OF THE GENERATION OF JESUS CHRIST, THE SON OF DAVID,' WHEN ABRAHAM IS EARLIER?
  • VI. WHY IS IT THAT THE ABOVE-MENTIONED APOSTLE MATTHEW DIVIDED ALL THE GENERATIONS INTO THREE PARTS?
  • VII. WHY, SINCE THERE ARE FORTY-ONE GENERATIONS, DOES THE EVANGELIST SEEM TO HAVE COUNTED FORTY-TWO? FOR WHAT DO THREE TIMES FOURTEEN MAKE BUT FORTY-TWO?
  • VIII.
  • VIIII.
  • X.
  • XI.
  • XII.
  • XIII.
  • XIIII.
  • XV.
  • XVI.
  • XVII. WHY DID THE SAVIOR, AFTER HIS BAPTISM, FAST FOR FORTY DAYS AND THEN HUNGER? FOR HE WHO FASTED FORTY DAYS, COULD HE NOT BY THEN HAVE CEASED TO HUNGER?
  • XVIII. IF 'THE LAW AND THE PROPHETS WERE UNTIL JOHN,' FROM WHOM THE KINGDOM OF HEAVEN WAS PROCLAIMED — FOR HE IS THE INITIATOR OF THE NEW PREACHING —, WHY DID HIS BAPTISM CEASE?
  • XVIIII. WHY ARE 'THE LAW AND THE PROPHETS' RIGHTLY SAID TO HAVE CEASED UNTIL JOHN? BECAUSE HE OF WHOM THEY PROPHESIED HAD NOW COME. WHY 'THE LAW UNTIL JOHN,' WHEN THE APOSTLE SAYS THAT WE OUGHT TO BE SUBJECT TO THE LAW? 'FOR THE THINGS THAT ARE,' HE SAYS, 'HAVE BEEN ORDAINED BY GOD.'
  • XX.
  • XXI.
  • XXII. THE SABBATH IS SURELY THE LAW, OR PART OF THE LAW: HOW THEN IS THE LAW NOT ABOLISHED, WHEN THE SABBATH HAS BEEN DISSOLVED, SINCE THE EVANGELIST SAYS: 'BECAUSE HE NOT ONLY BROKE THE SABBATH' AND THE REST?
  • XXIII. WHY THE SAVIOR CALLED HIS DISCIPLES SONS OF THUNDER, WHO WOULD RATHER SEEM TO BE CALLED SONS OF GOD? FOR THUNDERS ARE SAID TO BE PRODUCED BY THE COLLISION OF CLOUDS.
  • XXIIII.
  • XXV.
  • XXVI.
  • XXVII.
  • XXVIII. IT IS PLAIN THAT WHEN HE WAS BORN THE SAVIOR WAS CALLED THE SON OF GOD AND CHRIST: WHY THEN, AFTER HIS BAPTISM, DID THE TEMPTER APPROACH HIM SAYING: 'IF YOU ARE THE SON OF GOD,' AND THE REST?
  • XXVIIII. WHY DID THE SAVIOR RESIST THE DEVIL WHO WAS TEMPTING HIM IN NO OTHER WAY THAN BY EXAMPLES FROM THE LAW?
  • XXX.
  • XXXI.
  • XXXII. THE GOSPEL TESTIFIES THAT 'NO ONE HAS SEEN GOD': AGAINST THIS, JACOB AND MOSES AND ISAIAH ASSERT THAT THEY HAVE SEEN GOD. BUT SOMEONE SAYS: «NO ONE HAS SEEN THE FATHER». WHAT OF IT? IF THE SON WAS SEEN, THE FATHER TOO WAS SEEN, SINCE BOTH THE FATHER AND THE SON ARE ALIKE ONE GOD BOTH IN SUBSTANCE AND IN IMAGE, BECAUSE THE IMAGE OF THE TWO IS ONE AND, AS HE HIMSELF SAYS: 'WHOEVER SEES ME, SEES THE FATHER ALSO.' HOW THEN HAS NO ONE SEEN THE FATHER, GOD, WHEN THE SON SAYS THAT THE FATHER IS SEEN WHEN HE HIMSELF IS SEEN, SINCE THERE IS NOT ANOTHER GOD? IF THEN THERE IS NOT ANOTHER, HE HIMSELF, THE SAME, BECAUSE HE IS ONE, GOD HAS BEEN SEEN.
  • XXXIII. HOW IS IT THAT THE SAVIOR, TO THE FOREIGN WOMAN, THAT IS, THE CANAANITE, AT FIRST DENIED MERCY, WHEN HE DID NOT REFUSE THE BENEFIT OF GRANTING HEALTH BOTH TO THE FOREIGN CENTURION AND TO THE LEPER, WHOM JESUS HIMSELF CALLED A FOREIGNER?
  • XXXIIII.
  • XXXV.
  • XXXVI.
  • XXXVII.
  • XXXVIII.
  • XXXVIIII. THE APOSTLE PETER SAYS: 'CHRIST DIED FOR US', BUT THE APOSTLE PAUL ASSERTS THAT HE DIED ALSO FOR HIMSELF: 'HAVING BEEN MADE,' HE SAYS, 'OBEDIENT UNTO DEATH; FOR WHICH REASON GOD BESTOWED ON HIM A NAME, WHICH IS ABOVE EVERY NAME.' IF THIS IS SO, HE WILL SEEM TO HAVE BEEN IMPERFECT, WHO BY HIS OWN WORKS MADE AN INCREASE.
  • XL.
  • XLI.
  • XLII. JOHN TO THE LORD: 'ARE YOU THE ONE WHO IS TO COME, OR DO WE AWAIT ANOTHER?'
  • XLIII. HOW IS IT THAT, WHEN THE SAVIOR HAD HEALED ALMOST ALL BY A WORD, HE NEVERTHELESS RESTORED THE EYES OF THE BLIND MAN BY MEANS OF MUD MADE FROM SPITTLE?
  • XLIIII. HOW IS IT THAT, WHEN ABOUT TO PERFORM A WONDERFUL AND UNKNOWN MIRACLE, NAMELY WHEN ABOUT TO RAISE LAZARUS FROM THE DEAD, HE WEPT OR ASKED, AS IF UNAWARE, FOR THE PLACE WHERE HE HAD BEEN LAID?
  • XLV. HOW IS IT THAT ABOVE WE READ THAT HEROD HAD DIED, BUT BELOW, AND AFTER MANY YEARS, THAT HEROD KILLED JOHN, WHEN ABOVE, AFTER HEROD'S DEATH, JOHN OUTLIVED HIM?
  • XLVI.
  • XLVII.
  • XLVIII. WHY THE APOSTLE SAYS HE BECAME ALL THINGS TO ALL MEN, WHICH SEEMS TO BE THE ACT OF A FLATTERER AND A HYPOCRITE?
  • XLVIIII.
  • L. SINCE WE PROFESS THE SAVIOR TO HAVE BEEN BORN, WHY IS IT THAT THE APOSTLE SAYS HE WAS MADE FROM THE SEED OF DAVID, SINCE TO BE MADE IS ONE THING AND TO BE BORN ANOTHER?
  • LI. WHY DID THE APOSTLE SAY TO THE GALATIANS, WHOM THROUGHOUT THE WHOLE EPISTLE HE THUS REBUKES AND REPROVES: 'BE,' HE SAYS, 'AS I ALSO AM, FOR I AM AS YOU ARE'? IF THEN HE SHOWED HIMSELF SUCH AS THEY WERE, IT WAS SUPERFLUOUS TO SAY: 'BE AS I ALSO AM'; OR PERHAPS IN CERTAIN MATTERS HE HAD BEGUN TO BE AN IMITATOR OF THEM, AND IN SOME HE WISHES THEM TO BE IMITATORS OF HIMSELF?
  • LII. IN WHAT WAY ARE WE OF FREE JUDGMENT AND WILL, WHEN THE APOSTLE SAYS: 'THE FLESH LUSTS AGAINST THE SPIRIT, BUT THE SPIRIT AGAINST THE FLESH, SO THAT YOU DO NOT DO THE THINGS THAT YOU WOULD'? AND IF THE FLESH LUSTS AGAINST THE SPIRIT, IT IS EVIL; FOR THE SPIRIT SUGGESTS GOOD THINGS.
  • LIII. FOR WHAT REASON IS THE WISDOM OF THE FLESH AN ENEMY TO GOD, OR WHAT IS THAT WISDOM ITSELF, WHICH IS NOT SUBJECT TO THE LAW OF GOD?
  • LIIII.
  • LV. WHY IS IT THAT, ALTHOUGH JOHN THE BAPTIST HAD EARLIER BORNE WITNESS TO THE SAVIOR, HE AFTERWARD DOUBTED, SAYING THROUGH HIS DISCIPLES: 'ARE YOU HE WHO IS TO COME, OR DO WE LOOK FOR ANOTHER?'
  • LVI.
  • LVII. WHAT DOES THE APOSTLE MEAN WHEN HE SAYS TO THE GALATIANS: 'I MARVEL THAT YOU ARE SO QUICKLY TRANSFERRED FROM HIM WHO CALLED YOU INTO GRACE, TO ANOTHER GOSPEL, WHICH IS NOT ANOTHER? IF IT IS INDEED ANOTHER, IT IS NOT THE SAME; IF IT IS NOT THE SAME, HOW IS IT NOT ANOTHER?
  • LVIII. SINCE MANY SINS SEEM TO BE COMMITTED AGAINST THE BODY — FOR EVERYONE WHO DOES VIOLENCE TO HIMSELF IN ANY PART OF THE BODY CERTAINLY SINS AGAINST HIS OWN BODY; FOR THERE IS ONE WHO CASTRATES HIMSELF, THERE IS ONE WHO ENDS HIS LIFE WITH A NOOSE, THERE IS ONE WHO THRUSTS A SWORD INTO HIMSELF —, WHY DOES THE APOSTLE SAY: 'EVERY SIN,' HE SAYS, 'WHATEVER A MAN COMMITS, IS OUTSIDE THE BODY; BUT HE WHO FORNICATES SINS AGAINST HIS OWN BODY'?
  • LVIIII.
  • LX. WHY DID THE APOSTLE PAUL REBUKE PETER HIS FELLOW-APOSTLE, BECAUSE, 'FEARING THOSE WHO WERE OF THE CIRCUMCISION, HE WITHDREW HIMSELF' FROM THE GENTILES, WHEN HE HIMSELF ALSO, FEARING THOSE WHO WERE OF THE CIRCUMCISION, 'TOOK AND CIRCUMCISED' TIMOTHY, WHICH HE FORBADE TO BE DONE, AND THEREFORE IS HE HIMSELF ALSO TO BE REBUKED?
  • LXI. WHICH SPIRIT DOES THE APOSTLE ASSERT IS TO BE SAVED, WHEN HE SAYS THAT A MAN OF THIS KIND IS HANDED OVER TO SATAN FOR THE DESTRUCTION OF THE FLESH?
  • LXII. WHY DOES THE SAVIOR SAY: 'PRAY,' HE SAYS, 'THAT YOUR FLIGHT BE NOT IN WINTER OR ON THE SABBATH,' WHEN THE TIME OF THIS PERSECUTION CANNOT BE DEFERRED, SINCE THE APOSTLE SAYS: 'WHO SHALL BE REVEALED IN HIS OWN TIME,' AND IN THE ACTS OF THE APOSTLES: 'DETERMINING,' HE SAYS, 'THE TIMES AND THE BOUNDS OF THEIR HABITATION'? AND WHY IS IT NOT PERMITTED TO FLEE IN WINTER OR TO GO OUT ON THE SABBATH [DOES IT SIGNIFY]?
  • LXIII.
  • LXIIII.
  • LXV. WHAT DOES THE APOSTLE MEAN WHEN HE SAYS: 'NO ONE CAN SAY THE LORD JESUS EXCEPT IN THE HOLY SPIRIT'? CAN PHOTINUS THEN, WHO DENIES THAT CHRIST IS GOD, CONFESS OUR LORD JESUS CHRIST IN THE HOLY SPIRIT? AND CAN MARCION AND MANICHAEUS, WHO DENY THAT CHRIST CAME IN THE FLESH, SAY THE LORD JESUS CHRIST IN THE HOLY SPIRIT? OR HARLOTS AND THE FILTHY, SINCE THE HOLY SPIRIT DOES NOT DWELL IN A BODY SUBJECT TO SINS AND WISDOM DOES NOT ENTER INTO A MALEVOLENT SOUL?
  • LXVI. IF IN THE LAW NO ONE IS JUSTIFIED BEFORE GOD, WHY IS IT WRITTEN: 'CURSED IS EVERYONE WHO DOES NOT REMAIN IN ALL THE THINGS THAT ARE WRITTEN IN THE BOOK OF THE LAW, THAT HE SHOULD DO THEM'? IF MEN ARE JUSTIFIED BY FAITH AND NOT THROUGH THE LAW, WHY IS HE CURSED WHO HAS NOT FULFILLED THE LAW, SINCE IT DOES NOT AVAIL TOWARD RIGHTEOUSNESS?
  • LXVII. IF IN CHRIST ALL THE TREASURES OF WISDOM AND KNOWLEDGE ARE HIDDEN, HOW DOES THE SAME SAVIOR SAY THAT HE DOES NOT KNOW THE DAY AND HOUR OF THE JUDGMENT TO COME? BUT IF HE KNOWS AND SAYS THAT HE DOES NOT KNOW, HE SEEMS TO LIE.
  • LXVIII.
  • LXVIIII. THE SAVIOR SAYS: 'WHOEVER DOES NOT LEAVE ALL HIS POSSESSIONS', THAT IS, HOUSE AND FIELD AND THE REST, 'CANNOT BE MY DISCIPLE'; AND ON THE CONTRARY THE EVANGELIST SAYS: 'THERE CAME JOSEPH OF ARIMATHEA, A RICH MAN, WHO WAS HIMSELF ALSO A DISCIPLE OF JESUS, AWAITING THE KINGDOM OF GOD': HOW IS IT THAT THE EVANGELIST DECLARES HIM A DISCIPLE WHOM THE SAVIOR DENIED? FOR ZACCHAEUS TOO WAS RICH, AND CORNELIUS THE CENTURION WAS RICH, AND THE WOMEN WHO MINISTERED TO HIM FROM THEIR MEANS.
  • LXX. HOW IS IT THAT THE SAVIOR SAYS TO MARY, WHO WISHED TO TOUCH HIM OUT OF JOY: 'DO NOT TOUCH ME; FOR I HAVE NOT YET ASCENDED TO THE FATHER', WHEN HE IS READ TO HAVE BEEN BOTH TOUCHED AND WORSHIPED BY THE OTHER WOMEN?
  • LXXI. WHAT DOES THE SAVIOR MEAN WHEN HE SAYS: 'I AM THE DOOR; THOSE WHO WERE BEFORE ME ARE THIEVES AND ROBBERS'? THIS SAYING SEEMS TO STRIKE AT THE PROPHETS.
  • LXXII. THE APOSTLE SAYS THAT CHRIST DIED FOR ALL; FOR THUS HE SAYS: 'THEREFORE ALL ARE DEAD, AND HE DIED FOR ALL', BUT THE LORD HIMSELF SAYS: 'THE SON OF MAN CAME TO GIVE HIS LIFE AS A REDEMPTION FOR MANY': IN THIS WAY IT IS CONTRADICTORY.
  • LXXIII. HOW IS IT THAT DAVID SAYS: 'LET THEM BE CONFOUNDED AND ASHAMED WHO SAY TO ME: "WELL DONE, WELL DONE"', BUT THE LORD SAYS: 'WELL DONE, GOOD AND FAITHFUL SERVANT', AND SO FORTH? THAT WHICH DAVID TOOK AS A REPROACH AND AN EVIL, THIS THE SAVIOR SHOWS TO BE WORTHY OF GOOD MERITS?
  • LXXIIII.
  • LXXV. THE APOSTLE CALLS THE LAW GIVEN BY MOSES HOLY AND JUST AND GOOD AND SPIRITUAL, AND ELSEWHERE HE SAYS: 'FOR THE LAW WORKS WRATH' AND: 'WHERE THERE IS NO LAW, NEITHER IS THERE TRANSGRESSION'. FOR TO BE WITHOUT THESE IS SECURITY.
  • LXXVI. IF THE JEWS RECEIVED HARSH COMMANDMENTS ON ACCOUNT OF THEIR DISTRUST AND DISPARAGEMENTS, WHAT HAD THEIR CHILDREN SINNED, THAT THEY TOO SHOULD BE BOUND BY THESE COMMANDMENTS?
  • LXXVII. SINCE THE SAVIOR SAYS: 'I PRAY FOR THEM. FOR THOSE WHOM YOU HAVE GIVEN ME, I DO NOT PRAY FOR THE WORLD', BUT JOHN THE APOSTLE SAYS ON THE CONTRARY: 'WE HAVE', HE SAYS, 'AN ADVOCATE WITH THE FATHER, AN INTERCESSOR FOR OUR SINS, AND NOT ONLY FOR OURS, BUT FOR THE WHOLE WORLD': THIS SEEMS CONTRADICTORY.
  • LXXVIII. IN THE GOSPEL WE READ THAT THE ANGEL SAYS TO MARY THE MOTHER OF THE LORD THAT 'OF HIS KINGDOM', THAT IS, OF CHRIST'S, 'THERE WILL BE NO END', AND DANIEL SPEAKS IN THE SAME SENSE ABOUT THIS; FOR HE SAYS: THEN THERE WILL ARISE AN ETERNAL KINGDOM, WHICH WILL NEVER BE DESTROYED'. BUT ON THE CONTRARY THE APOSTLE SAYS OF THE LORD: 'WHEN HE HAS HANDED OVER', HE SAYS, 'THE KINGDOM TO GOD AND THE FATHER'. HOW WILL HE HAVE AN ETERNAL KINGDOM, WHICH IS SAID TO BE ABOUT TO BE HANDED OVER TO GOD AND THE FATHER?
  • LXXVIIII.
  • LXXX. WHAT NEED WAS THERE FOR THE APOSTLE, IN REBUKING THE GALATIANS, TO INSERT THIS — FOR TO THE GALATIANS, WHO AFTER THE GOSPEL WERE FLEEING BACK TO THE LAW, HE SAYS AMONG OTHER THINGS: 'FOR A MEDIATOR IS NOT OF ONE, BUT GOD IS ONE' —, AS IF THE GALATIANS WERE DENYING ONE GOD, SEEING THAT THEY HAD BEEN LED BY THIS VERY REASONING INTO THE LAW, NAMELY THAT THEY SHOULD BELIEVE IN ONE AND SINGULAR GOD, BUT THAT CHRIST HAD COME ONLY AS A MINISTER BY PREDESTINATION TO DISPENSE THE GIFT OF THE GRACE OF GOD?
  • LXXXI. THE SAVIOR, WHEN HE SAID THAT HE WOULD SUFFER AND RISE AGAIN AFTER THE THIRD DAY, ADDED: 'AND AFTER I HAVE RISEN, I WILL GO BEFORE YOU INTO GALILEE; THERE YOU WILL SEE ME'. AND THE ANGEL LIKEWISE TO THE WOMEN. YET HE IS FOUND TO HAVE BEEN SEEN BY THE WOMEN AND BY HIS DISCIPLES IN JERUSALEM.
  • LXXXII. PAUL THE APOSTLE INDICATES THAT ONE MUST NOT GRIEVE OVER THE DEAD; FOR TO GRIEVE IS THE MARK OF THOSE WITHOUT HOPE, AND YET HE HIMSELF SAYS OF EPAPHRODITUS: 'HE WAS SICK', HE SAYS, 'NEAR TO DEATH. BUT GOD HAD MERCY ON HIM; AND NOT ONLY ON HIM, BUT ALSO ON ME, LEST I SHOULD HAVE SORROW UPON SORROW'. HOW DOES HE FORBID GRIEVING, WHEN HE HIMSELF DECLARES THAT HE WOULD HAVE GRIEVED IF THE MAN HAD DIED?
  • LXXXIII. HOW IS IT THAT, WHEN THE APOSTLES HAD HEALED ALL THE SICK BROUGHT TO THEM, THEY YET GAVE NO REMEDY TO THEIR OWN SICK? FOR SURELY EPAPHRODITUS WOULD NOT HAVE BEEN ILL EVEN TO THE POINT OF DEATH, IF THE APOSTLE'S INTERCESSION HAD BEEN HEARD. FOR WHO WOULD DOUBT THAT THE APOSTLE OFTEN PRAYED FOR THIS AND DID NOT OBTAIN IT? FOR IF HE HAD BEEN HEARD, THE SICKNESS WOULD AT ONCE HAVE BEEN TAKEN AWAY.
  • LXXXIIII.
  • LXXXV.

The Book of Questions [of Saint Augustine] on the Old and New Testament, One Hundred and Twenty-Seven Questions in Number

I. WHAT IS GOD?

God is that which no conception attains. For He is more than whatever could be said or thought. Yet let us say something which, though it be unequal, may nonetheless by some reasoning accord with those things that seem worthy of God. For each and every nature surmises about God according to its own capacity, so that as greatly as nature is distant from nature, so greatly is one opinion distant from another as to what God is. For because He is above all things, it is necessary that He surpass the minds of all. For men, as far as they are able to extend the keenness of their mind, behold what God is by conception, not by definition; but the angels, who are superior to men, since they perceive something more about God, there is no doubt; the archangels, indeed, by that very fact perceive more amply; the cherubim and seraphim, however, which are said to be the powers nearest to God, perceive greater things concerning God, yet they do not comprehend utterly what God is, because no one knows the Father except the Son, nor does anyone know the Son except the Father.

Therefore God is, as it appears to men, a spirit simple in nature, light unapproachable, invisible, inestimable, infinite, perfect, needing nothing, eternal, immortal in every way, from whom all things obtained their beginning; to be venerated, to be loved, to be feared, outside of whom there is nothing, or rather in whom are all things whatsoever that are above, below, the highest and the lowest; almighty, all-holding, truly rich in all things, because there is nothing which is not His; good, just, merciful: good, because He caused to exist things that were not; just, because the things He made, so that they might advance, were released to their own free will of choice — for since they are not so perfect that they cannot fall, He decreed that the seeds of the law be within them, naturally adding the aid of the manifested law, so that its authority might be a source of advancement for men —; but merciful, because He does not readily requite those who sin, but bears with them so that He may pardon them when they are converted. He is also severe, so that by terror the things which have been well established by Him may be preserved, lest negligence beget the ruin of life; and, not to pass over what is more wonderful, so great is His clemency that, having suffered insults from those whom He made, He endures them and is the first to call them to peace. Is this not of greater power than to have founded the creature? And if He were to remain in this, His excessive goodness would harm the creature. Whence He wills to be at one time loved, at another time feared, lest those straying from Him utterly perish. Hence it is that, lest His patience be thought altogether to be despised — not to His own harm, but to ours — He says: I have held my peace; shall I always hold my peace?

And so, the good God—all the things that he made are good. Whence then evil? There is no evil except the transgression of the good, when things not permitted are presumed upon or permitted things are done in a disordered way, so that what is commanded in one place is done in another: as when what is permitted in a wife is done in a harlot; and what was to be offered to God is offered to the devil; and when, because one takes not his own but another's; and when, though it is lawful for a transgressor to be killed, an innocent man is killed. No nature, therefore, is proven to be evil. But the will is an accident of nature, conceived from causes, which is moved badly when it exceeds due measure, so that it carries out those things which are not of its own nature. And the causes of transgression arise from the senses, when we see or hear something badly. This thing produces such error, because man is not God, who alone cannot err.

The nature of men, therefore, has been released to its own free choice, so that it can do what it wills, so that, if practice makes better the good of its own nature, it may be a matter of honor, but if it weakens its own vigor, one of this kind may be held worthy of reproach. For it does what is against itself. It is no small thing that has been granted to man, that when he follows what is right, he may rejoice in himself through that whereby he sees himself made better by his own work, or at least may reckon it to himself when, though he was able, he gave no effort to make himself better by good things. But if man were not in his own power, he would have been subject to necessity, so that he would have neither the glory of a good work nor the punishment of an evil one, but would have been one of the beasts.

Since, therefore, we have been made capable of both—so that through negligence we may fail, if what we ought to hear and see well we hear badly, that is, contrary to nature and reason, but through vigilance we may guard the good of nature, and we cannot always be on guard, because, as I said, we have been made capable of both—if we sin, we are not yet condemned, unless we fail again, being now as it were destroyers. For whoever has sinned once ought to restore himself lest he sin anew, lest he be equal to the one who had conquered him, so that if again he does not sin, he may now be held superior, because, once struck down, he has twice triumphed. This is justice: that, since there is a struggle in the world, whoever is more inclined toward not sinning should be crowned.

Nothing, therefore, in the work of God is evil; and if by some certain things are called evil, such as poison, such as darkness—because, indeed, our bodies cannot bear the force of poison, it is called evil, as though they could bear fire or water—and iron or lead. Because it is far distant from gold, it will be called evil. For by comparison with light they condemn darkness, though they know it to be necessary in its own place, like lead or an earthen vessel. For assuredly they give rest after labor.

Therefore everyone who wrestles in the world ought so to strive that he not withdraw defeated in a hard struggle and become guilty, restoring himself scarcely or slowly, and perhaps amid these things his end may come, and he may depart hence with sin. For he who strives back with all his strength, if he happens to be struck down, falls like a man, nor does anyone grow angry at him, but by a certain encouragement restores his spirit. For he saw that he had set before himself the purpose of conquering, and he hopes that such a one can advance to victory, whom his enemy struck down not without wearying himself. For he who is easily conquered has no spirit of resisting, nor is he conquered, but he consents. This man sins more bitterly; one of this kind is scarcely to be admitted to pardon, one who has the desire of transgressing. For he who takes thought that he not sin, even if he should sin, does not sin harshly. For upon those who love, lesser sins sometimes creep in unawares. For the lesser they are, the more subtle, and while they are despised, they are not avoided. For the greater ones appear from afar, and through this he who sins in the greater ones, the crime is of his will.

Indeed, since above we said that sins take their origin from the senses, when against the command of the law or reason we look upon or hear something — that is, if, seeing the sun, we should think it ought to be adored on account of its beauty, then we see wrongly, because it pertains to the injury of the common Creator that what is owed to him alone should be attributed to a creature, seeing indeed that it has been forbidden by him through the law. Or when we see bodies well composed and comely, or if we covet something of our neighbor's, we look upon these otherwise than the law commands, then there occurs the sin which is called evil. But perhaps it may be said: 'nothing beautiful ought to have been made, lest we should sin,' so that our safeguarding might rest upon the deformity of others, and there should be no iron, lest homicides be committed from it, nor should a lamp be in use, lest thieves use its light for breaking in — so that what is greatly useful to all should be lacking on account of the empty talk of certain men, when it is established that we always look upon all things and yet do not always covet, because it is not their fault, but ours, when we are negligent. And this is established by the interval of creation, because we are not what God is. But thus we hear wrongly, if hearing that idols are gods we consent, or if we lend our ear to those who sing base things. But then we hear well, if hearing about God that he is one we take delight. But if anyone, hearing something against the law, assents, he sins: this will be to hear wrongly.

II. WHY GOD MADE THE WORLD.

He made it, because he is a maker; or let it be denied, if he is not. But the works themselves make manifest that he is. He made, therefore, that there might be what before was not, because without doubt it is better to be than not to be. But it is said: 'was there some empty space where he might make, or what was there before, where he made?' This vessel of election resolved this in few words. For he said, when the discourse was about God: in him we live and are moved and are, that is, that all things are in God, because he is everywhere and before all things alone, eternal, invisible to every creature.

And lest we should seem to have passed over the mystery, or rather to have been ignorant of why the world was made, we say that the apostasy of the devil dragged many angels—that is, spiritual powers—with it into transgression, while he wished to secure a kingdom for himself by impious presumption. This the prophet Isaiah signifies when he says: How is Lucifer fallen from heaven, who used to rise in the morning? that is, who appeared brighter than the rest. For he was as it were the prince of many, among whom he was more illustrious, and with whose fellowship he descended to the impious contest. For seeing beneath himself many spiritual powers—since indeed in the paradise of God he was more excellent in the knowledge of the heavenly mystery—puffed up by that very exaltation he wished to be called God, by that same reasoning, indeed, by which even in the present life we see certain men imitating his example, who, gathered together by the display of soldiery around themselves and lifted up—with their retainers furnishing in this matter the kindling of conspiracy—have wished to claim sovereignty for themselves.

Hence it is that God, in order to destroy his presumption not by power but by reason, established matter, which was a confusion of things, out of which He might make the world. For the things which had been confused together, once distinguished, produced this ornament which we see. For when the substances had been separated from one another, by their being fitted together it is called "world" (mundus), because each single thing, set apart from another, came forth into an ordered arrangement, so that here man, placed and created out of the higher and lower things—that is, out of the heavenly and the earthly—might show forth the lordship of the one God not only by voice but also by image, whereby he was made one by the one God, from whom the rest might arise. For therefore the One made one, in order to teach that all things are from One, and through this that God is one, so that the higher creature, to its own confounding, might learn the truth in man, who was formed from earth.

From this the devil became the enemy of man; for he perceived that man had been made for his accusation. Whence by his subtlety he brought it about that he might lead him into the same transgression into which he himself had fallen, so that he might make his accuser a sharer of his own damnation. For by transgression he promised him deity, in aspiring to which he himself had been cast down. And because every nature is free from crime, names come from what befalls—for the thing comes first, afterwards its signification—and through this "satan" and "devil" are names composed from his act, so that it is the signification not of his nature but of his will.

And so, in order that the purpose of God, which he decreed in the matter of created man, might stand, and that the deed of the devil, through which he encompassed man's ruin, might avail toward the heaping up of his guilt, Christ deigned to come from the sacred seats to the earth, so that he might both free man from the sentence of transgression and display the future perdition of the devil, lest anyone should imitate his deed. For this reason the apostle John said: for this the Son of God came, that he might destroy the works of the devil. But if he were evil by nature, to promise him punishment would be the mark either of a madman or of an unjust person. For who would accuse him whom he sees to do nothing otherwise than his nature allows? Can one be angry at fire because it burns, or at water because it chills, since it assuredly does this not by will but by nature? Whence the devil too, if he were evil by nature, would not have will. For neither would he be able to discriminate, but he would plunge himself upon all in one and the same manner, like a blind man.

But furthermore, he does this with a certain discernment; for he spares those who do his will, he feigns indifference toward certain newcomers, against those wishing to flee to God's help he sets up stumbling-blocks and impediments, he lays snares for the servants of God, and toward those who are more ready in obedience to him he is the more hostile. Whence it is manifest that his will is in the fault. For which reason the apostle Peter says: be sober and watchful, because your adversary the devil goes about like a roaring lion, seeking whom he may devour. He does not seek the gentiles, he does not seek the Jews, he does not seek those of evil life and conduct, but he seeks the servants of God and of Christ, whom he knows to be enemies to himself, because they condemn his deed and his presumption.

Finally, once the law had been given, he blazed the more with envy against those who were under the law, knowing that the teachings of the law hand down one God and a good manner of life to men. Therefore, if he is thought to do these things naturally, he cannot be established as guilty, because he does this which belongs to his nature and which he is able to do, and he does not do what he cannot, because it does not belong to his nature; and so he is neither to be praised nor to be condemned. He is not to be praised, because the things he does are harmful; but he is not to be condemned, because he does these things not by will but by the impulse of nature. For we know that some, suddenly made insane, have harmed many with sword, club, stones, and bites, and that some have even killed; yet that when they were caught by contrivance and brought before the tribunals, they were by no means made guilty, for the reason that they had done these things not by will but by some impelling force I know not what, without knowing it. For how is he established as guilty who does not know what he has done? So too the devil, if he does not know the good, why is he judged to be worthy of damnation, seeing that he does not do what he does not know? Nay rather, if it could be so, he would have to be praised, because he does what he knows.

Now, we are rightly held guilty of the matter, because we do something other than what we know we ought to do. But since throughout all Scripture we see the devil constituted as guilty, and for that reason we read that Gehenna has been prepared for him, we know that he is to be condemned by the laws, because, although he knew and was able to do good, he did evil. For God, who is just, would not condemn him because he had not done good which he had not known, or because he had done evil which he had known. And so I think it has been made clear that no nature ought to be called evil, because every evil, as has become plain, arises from the will, which befalls a nature through the senses.

III. WHAT NEED WAS THERE TO SET FORTH THE BEGINNING OF THE WORLD AND THE ORDER OF CREATION THROUGH MOSES, AND NOT BEFORE?

It ought not to have been described earlier, because up to then there was not, from this cause, so great an error among men. But when the error grew in the human race, so that even the sons of Israel in Egypt heard, contrary to this exposition, teachings handed down by the philosophers of the Egyptians — by whom Moses too had been instructed in all Egyptian learning — which asserts that a certain Sacla fashioned this world through evil angels, and that this same one is also seen to be the prince of the world, that is, Satan (a doctrine which Marcion followed and rushed to his death; for the Manicheans too say that man was made by the same Sacla, not this world — being more foolish than the rest; for whereas it is agreed that the world was fashioned for the sake of man, they say the world was made by God, though from another's material, but that man was created by the adversary, so that the one set up a master in another's house) — it was therefore necessary that Moses, in order to expose and remove this error, should make manifest that God is the author of the world and of man as fashioned. For having received authority through the signs and prodigies which he did, he taught without doubt that this was true which he was handing down with signs as witnesses. For who would not believe him, whose signs were so great in the things he did? Finally, hence it is that those who hold views against this teaching are known to be in error, because they strive to allege their assertions with bare words.

And so, in order to teach that nothing is coeternal with God, he sets forth the very order of created things, so that, while he first records the lesser things as made, but afterward the greater ones, none of these may be held to be uncreated; for the things that are lesser in time are greater in power, so that, if those greater things should suppose themselves to have precedence in respect of time, they may be refuted by the very weakness whereby they are made subject to the things that come after; or if these later things, by presuming upon their power, should claim primacy for themselves, they may be humbled by their very lateness — so that none of these may be seen to be anything but subject from the beginning. Indeed, first heaven was made, and earth; then light, which in its function is day; afterward the firmament, which was called heaven, and the gatherings of the waters, which he called seas, so that the earth might appear, in which it might be possible to dwell. But the earth, which he says was made after heaven, he does not wish to be understood as earth alone, but he signified matter, that is, all the lower things, which went forth into the whole outward form of the world. But the heaven that was made in the beginning he maintains to be not this carnal heaven, but that upper heaven which is spiritual, so that, when he says that heaven was made first, then earth, he might mark that in heaven all invisible things and in earth all visible things were created by God. For he comprehends the highest and the lowest of the whole of nature, so that whatever is in between may without doubt be believed to have been made. But the luminaries, which he established for governing the world, he affirms to have been made on the fourth day, so that, by however much they are great in power, by so much they may be inferior in time. But man he set up on the sixth day, so that he might bring the inhabitant into a house already made.

Hence it is that what displeases certain people was said: and God saw the light, that it is good. So that, because all things were said to have been made by an evil one and could not be believed to be good, Moses, in order to prove that the things which were made are good, showed that the things which He made were pleasing to God Himself, so that he might make guilty the one to whom they should be displeasing. For how could He fail to know the light, who said: let there be light, and light was made? Does anyone make what he does not know? And the light, once made, was pleasing to Him who made it. What craftsman does not rejoice in his own work? If it was said: God saw the light, that it is good, even so there are those who say 'it is evil'; what, then, if it had been left without testimony?

Therefore, having described the fashioning of the world and the origin of the first man, the line of descent held to the race of Seth, who was granted in place of Abel, and it came in order down to Abraham the father of the Jews, in order to show that Abraham believed in this God who is the maker of the world, and that this same God gave the Law, in which the Christ who was to come was promised, who would free the human race from the dominion of the devil. From these things our faith is proven reasonable; for the described lineage bears witness to this God, because the race of Christians exists from the beginning. For from Seth the son of Adam one comes to Enoch, from Enoch to Noah, from Noah to Abraham, from Abraham one descends to David, and from David, from Mary by the Holy Spirit, Christ is born. Therefore all those before, as many as had faith in the one God whom the Savior preached, must rightly be called Christians; for from the beginning the Savior was promised as one who would come. Whence in the Apocalypse he says: the Lamb who was slain from the foundation of the world. And so Christianity has always existed. For all these, whom I have mentioned above, from the first man created in the world, through whom the line of descent is drawn down to the Savior, had faith in this God, of whom Christ spoke, saying: And this is eternal life, that they may know thee the only and true God, and Jesus Christ whom thou hast sent. It can be said, on the contrary: "If Christianity existed before, what knowledge came through Christ?" This advance of understanding the coming of Christ conferred, because it revealed the mystery of the one God who had been preached, and demonstrated what belongs to which person, and, to fulfill the righteousness of the Law, added the things that had been reserved.

IIII. WHY DID HE NOT GIVE THE LAW AT THE BEGINNING?

First, the Law, formed in letters, ought not to have been given, because it is in a certain manner implanted in nature itself, and the knowledge of the Creator, handed down by descent, was not hidden. For who does not know what befits a good life, or is ignorant that what he does not wish to be done to himself ought by no means to be done to another? But when the natural law had vanished, crushed by the habit of wrongdoing, then it was fitting that it be made manifest, so that in the Jews all might hear it—not because it had been utterly obliterated, but they lacked its greatest authority: idolatry was pursued; the fear of God was not in the lands; fornication was practiced; men were greedy with covetousness concerning their neighbor's property. Therefore the Law was given, so that both the things that were known might have authority and the things that had begun to lie hidden might be made manifest. For we find that before Moses sins were not only not hidden, but were even punished. For which reason many are also found to have been righteous; for knowing God as an avenger they feared to sin. And when this had begun to be neglected, it was necessary for the natural law to be revealed, so that all might know by open reasoning that the Lord would demand an account of human deeds. Although it is read that punishment was carried out through the flood and upon Sodom and Gomorrah, yet the forgetfulness of antiquity had covered these things, whence through Moses they were called to remembrance, for the sake of terror, to correct discipline and to reform faith in God. Wherefore the Apostle also says: the law is not laid down for the righteous, but for the unrighteous, for those who worship idols, for fornicators, and such things.

Now let us consider whether it is fitting for those who, hearing of God's judgment, laugh at its being to come — whether it will profit or harm, whether it is fortified by truth or lacks reason. A law indeed has been given to the world, but we see that it fails in the case of many: it does not therefore seem just. Why is it that here sinners are safe through their power, others make sport of the laws, the poor are oppressed, an accusation is framed against the just, those who act well are held in reproach, the pious are in want, the wicked flourish, the unjust and the corrupt are held in honor, the greedy and the plunderers grow rich, the judge is for sale? Does it not seem unjust if the Founder of things does not call these things to account — that those who here have been unjustly oppressed should be relieved, and those who by living well have suffered want should be rewarded, and those who for the sake of justice were held in reproach should be honored; but those who through their power despised the laws or mocked them by evasion, pursuing iniquity, so glorious in these things that they seemed to insult justice itself, should be humbled and confounded and subjected to torments in the sight of those in whose evils and contempt they rejoiced, so that they too, glad at the punishment of those men, may give thanks to God, with whom alone respect of persons ceases?

V. WHY WAS ABEL'S SACRIFICE ACCEPTED AND CAIN'S REFUSED?

This very thing can be gathered from the words of the reading itself, since the history is not veiled by any art of letters. For in this very passage the language of Scripture shows Abel to be prudent and devout, but Cain negligent and improvident and thereby less devout. Abel therefore chose the better of his flocks, which he might offer to God the Creator, so that of the very things he had created he might offer Him the choicest, whereby he would prove both his own dedication and its merit, so as to show both his own reverence and God as the author. This Cain, like a boor, could not perceive. For, plunging his whole mind into the earth, he could not lift the eyes of his mind to heaven, so as to look upon what might be worthy of the Creator; for he offered God gifts of whatever sort.

This same cause is also detected among the Jews of crooked mind. For they were often rebuked when they improvidently offered their gifts on the altar of God — gifts that would not seem worthy even of men — as the Lord says: You offer me the blind and the one-eyed; I will not receive these from your hands. Offer them to your overseer or your governor, if he will accept them, since it is agreed among all that the greatest gifts ought to be offered to a person of high rank. And therefore Cain's gifts were refused, as God says to him: Why are you saddened, and why has your countenance fallen? Have you not sinned, if you offer rightly, but do not divide rightly? Be still. Unto you shall be its turning, and you shall rule over it.

You see, then, that division falls into sin. Since he did not consider what would be worthy of God, he reserved the better things for his own uses. And so he was not blamed because he made an offering, but because he offered unworthy things; nor was he condemned on that account, but rather admonished to amend the deed. For unto thee, He says, shall be its turning, and thou shalt rule over it, that is, 'since I do not accept it, the gift offered by you has turned back to your own dominion,' so that henceforth he might know what he was to do. From this, envy blazed up so that he killed his brother — so that he who had first shown righteousness might be slain by the unrighteous man, and an evil example be given to men. For he was so blinded by the rivalry of jealousy that not only did he give no thanks — for the fact that he had not been made guilty, but had also learned how to amend this —, but he even added something graver, by which he deserved to be condemned.

Such is the case of the improvident and parricidal Cain, as is also that of the wicked servant, who, though it had been overlooked by his lord, becoming ungrateful, went out and was throttling his fellow servant, so that both for his past misdeed overlooked to him and for the impiety committed against his fellow servant he might be condemned as inexcusable. And yet Cain was not condemned for the present, but, confounded and guilty, he was dismissed under terror upon the earth, so that, if he should repent, he might be pardoned. Finally, fearing lest someone kill him for this deed, he says to God: My case is greater than that I should be left. If thou castest me out this day from thy face, I will also hide myself from the face of the earth, and I shall be groaning and trembling upon the earth. And it shall come to pass, that everyone who findeth me shall slay me. Cain, terrified by the words of the righteous judge God, fears to be despised by God, so that he thinks he ought to flee even from the sight of men, being certain that whoever lives with God angry can be slain even by man. But what did the Lord answer him? Not so, He says — that is, 'I have not sent you back to this, though you do not deserve to live, so that you may be slain by someone, but so that you may groan and tremble, as one who first gave an evil example upon the earth, since the fruit from the ground did not answer to your labors.' And so, everyone who slayeth Cain, He says, shall pay seven vengeances. This sentence shows that Cain was to be justly condemned. For when he saw a law given under such a threat, that no one should imitate his deed, he began to fear more, knowing what evil he had committed.

Seven vengeances, therefore, He promises, if anyone should aspire to this crime, so that, seeing from this deed that Cain had been made guilty — and while there was as yet no manifestation of the law — he might know that he would be punished with a sevenfold penalty if he did not avoid this, so that the knowledge of the law would add six blows above what Cain had deserved, so that with Cain's blow the vengeances would be numbered as seven. By this number also are to be rewarded those who, having left all things, follow the Lord and in the future will have eternal life; this is the sign that God set upon Cain, that no one who found him should slay him. For a law was laid down concerning the parricide, that if anyone had committed a homicide — since every parricide is a homicide — he would be seven times more guilty than Cain had been, so that by this severity the rest, being terrified, might restrain themselves from this crime.

VI. IF LAMECH KILLED CAIN, AS IS SUPPOSED?

They think this in vain, who suppose that Lamech spoke about Cain: I have slain a man to my wounding, and a young man to my hurt. For Lamech had already been born in the fifth generation from Cain, that is, from Methuselah, the great-great-grandson of Cain. But Lamech mentions this for the purpose of showing that one who has sinned under a manifest law is to be bound more severely. And through this, if after Cain vengeance was taken sevenfold on his imitator, how much more is vengeance to be taken on him whom neither the deed of Cain and its rebuke, nor the sentence pronounced after him, terrified into turning his will away from so impious and cruel a crime! After Cain, then, Lamech committed a homicide, who without doubt, according to those things which were said above, paid seven vengeances. And he shows what was going to happen after Lamech to the one who would follow this example, saying: but of Lamech seventy-sevenfold — because a repentance does not follow an evil deed, he is struck with the blows of seventy-seven wounds. Whence also the Savior commanded that forgiveness be granted even to one sinning seventy-sevenfold, provided, however, that he has been converted.

But lest it be thought that another committed homicide after Cain before Lamech, because he said: of Cain vengeance was taken, as though it had already been done. But how could Lamech say of himself that vengeance had been taken on him, when the homicide was still recent, which he had confessed that he had committed, since it is established that every deed carries its sentence with it? For when there is no other hope, except that which is known to be deserved by the completed deed, the future is held as accomplished. Finally, it was said to Adam: on the day you eat, you shall die the death, and certainly they did not die at once, but after a long interval of time; but because the hope of immortality had already been lost, the future death was called present, because this began to be held in expectation. Therefore Lamech confesses that he killed a young man, and Cain, as has become clear, could not reach up to this time, or if he did reach it — which is impossible — he was an old man.

VII. WHICH TEN WORDS WERE GIVEN ON THE TABLETS, OR HOW MANY WORDS DID EACH TABLET HAVE?

He called the ten pronouncements ten words, because the Savior too signified a thought by "word" when he said, among other things, to the Jews: I too ask you one word; answer me: the baptism of John, whence was it, from heaven or from men? This thought he called a "word." In like manner also on the two tablets ten words are said to have been written, which are ten thoughts. Finally he says: let there not be for you other gods besides me — this is the first word — and he added: you shall not make for yourself any likeness of the things which are in heaven above and on the earth below, nor in the water which is under the earth. Then he added thirdly: you shall not take the name of the Lord your God in vain; for the Lord will not cleanse the one who takes his name in vain, that is, you shall not take the name of the Lord your God in a lie, so that you perjure yourself through it. Then in the fourth place he says: you shall keep the sabbaths of the Lord your God, and you shall not do on it any servile work. These are four words out of the ten; these pertain properly to the Lord; these are written on the first tablet.

Then in the second tablet these things are contained: the first word is: honor your father and mother; the second: you shall not kill; the third: you shall not commit fornication; the fourth: you shall not steal; the fifth: you shall not bear false witness; the sixth: you shall not covet anything of your neighbor's, and such things. That these were written on the second tablet the apostle Paul proves when he says: honor your father and mother, which is the first commandment with a promise. How would it be first, unless he had begun with it on the second tablet? And he said 'with a promise' for this reason, because he immediately subjoined: that you may be long-lived upon the earth and that it may be well with you. This is the promise made to those who keep the commandments. And so you have both the commandments distinguished and their number completed and what things and how many are written on each tablet.

VIII. WHY, WHEN MOSES CAME DOWN FROM THE MOUNTAIN WITH THE TABLETS, DID HE HAVE A COUNTENANCE SPLENDID AND UNBEARABLE?

Having received power over sinners, he came down from the mountain with honor with a glorious face. For the law was given against sinners. Moses therefore, because he had not sinned, appeared glorious to such a degree that he could not be looked upon by sinners. For it was shown in him that sinners do not merit to gaze upon the glory of God. For after the image of the molten calf and the breaking of the tablets, on which the law had been given, Moses again ascending the mountain with the tablets, on which, when he came down having received the law, his face was made glorious, so that the children of Israel could not gaze upon his countenance, nor Aaron, because he too had sinned; but with a veil interposed he spoke to them, so that they should be for so long unworthy of the glory of God, as long as they were turned about in sins.

Whence the apostle says: when he shall have been converted to the Lord, the veil shall be taken away, so that, being washed by the gift of God, they might become worthy to gaze upon the glory of God. For in the breaking of the tablets, which he had received before, he signified the reprobate people of the Jews, in that, being zealous for sins, they were going to be unworthy of the promise of God. But in that the law was repeated, another future people was signified, for whom the law given on the mountain would be of profit.

VIIII. IF GOD MADE ALL THINGS GOOD AND VERY GOOD, HOW IS IT THAT HE SAYS TO NOAH: 'OF THE CLEAN AND THE UNCLEAN BRING WITH YOU INTO THE ARK,' WHEN IN AN ABSOLUTE SENSE THE UNCLEAN CANNOT BE CALLED GOOD?

By reason of the fact that words have a manifold sense, they give rise to questions. For if they are referred to the matter at issue, there will be no question, because through their order the things themselves will disclose themselves. For sometimes we call 'common' that which is undivided, sometimes that which is unclean; for in two ways is a thing called 'common.' Thus the apostle Peter says: common, he says, and unclean never entered into my mouth, and the apostle Paul says: everything, he says, which is not of faith is sin, and elsewhere: the law, he says, is not of faith, and yet it is not sin. You see therefore that one and the same word does not always signify the same thing.

Therefore, when something is called (unclean), one must consider for what reason it is called so, because sometimes a thing is called unclean in comparison with better things, and sometimes it is referred to filthy deeds, so that it is understood as evil. No substance, then, is evil, because the things that are thought unclean by their substance are unclean in comparison with more beautiful things. For even bread is called unclean. And oil and lead are unclean in comparison with gold, and the raven in comparison with the peacock; and, although they are members of one body, some are called honorable and others dishonorable, though they are known not to be evil. And so all things are good in their own nature, because they are useful.

X. WHEN GOD SAYS TO ABRAHAM CONCERNING THE SONS OF ISRAEL THAT IN THE FOURTH GENERATION THEY WOULD COME OUT FROM THE POWER OF THE EGYPTIANS, HOW IS IT THAT, ON THE CONTRARY, THE LAW SAYS: 'IN THE FIFTH GENERATION THE SONS OF ISRAEL CAME OUT FROM THE LAND OF EGYPT'? IT SEEMS VERY MUCH A CONTRADICTION.

As far as the words are concerned, it seems to be a contradiction; but if the sense is sought out, it will be found to be not discordant. For the Law speaks in such a way that it can be understood by the diligent and attentive, so that the reasoning of the truth reveals itself not to the careless but to the earnest. For indeed God said: in the fourth generation, and Moses wrote: in the fifth generation, although Moses reported both, and it is impossible for him to deceive, in whom so great a power has worked. And on this account the sense must be investigated, because divine Scripture says nothing idly or improvidently. And so there are two parts, which each of them recorded. For God signified the four generations that were born in Egypt; but Moses, adding to these one more, from which these took their origin when they had entered into Egypt, says: in the fifth generation the sons of Israel came out. For he embraced together the generation that entered into Egypt and the four that were born there. For from Abraham up to the coming out of the sons of Israel from Egypt there are eight generations. For for two hundred and fifteen years from the promise made to Abraham they dwelt in Canaan, and for two hundred and fifteen in Egypt.

These are the years which the Apostle comprehends when he says to the Galatians: after four hundred and thirty years the Law was made. Therefore these four generations were born in Canaan, that is, one in Isaac, the second in Jacob, the third in Levi, the fourth in Gershon and Kohath and Merari. But when the sons of Israel had entered into Egypt, Kohath begot Amram — this is the first generation made in Egypt —; and Amram begot Aaron and Moses and Miriam, which is the second generation made in Egypt; and Aaron begot Eleazar and his brothers, which is the third generation; and Eleazar begot Phinehas in the fourth generation. These are the four generations begotten in Egypt. Whence God says to Abraham: your seed will be a stranger, and they will oppress them with servitude; but I will free them, in the fourth generation they will come out from there. See whether it is not plain that God signified nothing other than what was done in Egypt. But Moses, in order to include also that generation which entered into Egypt with its father Jacob, from which these four have their origin, said: in the fifth generation the sons of Israel came out from the land of Egypt.

XI. IF THE WILL OF A RIGHTEOUS MAN IS GOOD, HOW IS IT THAT ISAAC BLESSED NOT ESAU WHOM HE WISHED, BUT JACOB WHOM HE DID NOT WISH?

The will of a righteous man, as far as pertains to his own conscience, is good; but as far as pertains to foreknowledge, it is untouched by adverse things. For God alone is the one who judges concerning things to come. And on this account Isaac, being righteous, thought that his elder son ought rather to be blessed, insofar as it is fitting according to present humanity. But God, who is the knower of hidden things, showed that the younger deserved the blessing, so that in the blessing he might show the benefit to be not of man but of God, and that, because it is the dignity of an office and not the merit of a man, the blessing of God follows. Finally it was said by God in Numbers to Moses and Aaron the priests: But you, place my name upon the sons of Israel; I the Lord will bless them, so that the tradition might pour out grace to men through the ministry of the one ordained, and that the will of the priest could neither harm nor profit, but rather the merit of the one asking for the blessing.

But how great is the dignity of the priestly order, let us observe from this. It was said moreover concerning the most wicked Caiaphas, the slayer of the Savior, among other things: But this he did not say of himself, but since he was the high priest of that year, he prophesied. By this it is shown that the spirit of graces does not follow the person, whether of the worthy or the unworthy, but the ordination of the tradition, so that, although someone may be of good merit, he nevertheless cannot bless unless he has been ordained, so that he may exhibit the office of the ministry. But it belongs to God to bestow the effect of the blessing.

XII. WHY DID ABRAHAM RECEIVE CIRCUMCISION AS THE SIGN OF HIS FAITH?

If you are willing to observe, you will see that what you think to be at variance with reason is not incongruous. For believing that he would have a son, in whom all the nations would be blessed and from whom holiness was to arise, he received the sign in that part through which the begetting of children takes place and ceases, so that it might be holier. But if to some it seems a disfigurement, let them consider that Abraham rejoiced in it and that his sons were glorious by this testimony. For Achior indeed, one of the leaders of the gentiles, seeing that there was such great power in the God of Abraham that he beheaded Holofernes, the commander of the army of the Assyrians, whose might the whole earth trembled at, by his own sword through the hand of a woman, of his own accord circumcised himself, judging that by this very thing dignity had been sought for himself. Does he not display it before himself, if anyone has lost an eye or some member for the name of Christ? Does he not thrust that very part before human faces, so that he may appear glorious? For to lose something for a time for the sake of faith is to make a gain.

So too Abraham, receiving the sign of his faith, was not disfigured but improved. Yet spiritually he signified this: that the mist of the flesh was to be circumcised from the hearts of men through faith in Christ, because carnal error stood in the way, spreading a darkness over human hearts, so that they would not recognize their Creator. But Abraham, because it was promised that from his seed the future Christ would come, who would wipe away this darkness, was for that reason circumcised, because he believed that he would have a son through whom this error would be cut off.
