It is therefore the person of God the Father who says: Let us make; and of the Son who makes man to the image of God: whether to the Father's image or to his own makes no difference, since the image of both is one. The Son therefore made man through the Holy Spirit. For just as the Father is said to make through the Son, so also the Son makes through the Holy Spirit, as he himself says: For I cast out demons by the Spirit of God. Therefore the image of the three is one, since, whether the Father or the Son or the Holy Spirit, God is one. And through this man was made one to the image of the one God. Now man is the image of God in this respect, that, just as there is one God in the heavens, from whom all spiritual things subsist, so there should be one man on earth, from whom the rest would have their carnal origin.

To some, however, it seems that man was made the image of God in respect of dominion, because he said: and let him have dominion over the fish of the sea and the birds of the air and the whole earth, since these things are seen to be subjected not only to the man but also to the woman, who it is agreed does not have the image of God. But this indeed lacks reason in a twofold way; for by this reasoning it is asserted that God did not say to the Son: Let us make man to our image and likeness, but to the heavenly dominions, which the Apostle mentions; and if man has the image of God in dominion, it is granted also to the woman, so that she too is the image of God, which is absurd. For how can it be said of the woman that she is the image of God, when it is agreed that she is subjected to the dominion of the man and has no authority? For she can neither teach nor be a witness nor give a pledge nor judge: how much less rule!

XLVI. ON SAMUEL.

There are certain people among us who—partly occupied with worldly affairs, partly less diligent concerning the sacred Scriptures—suffer from an error, thinking that Samuel was a priest, that is, that he had his origin from Aaron, from whose progeny the Lord God established that priests should be born, not made. Nor was it permitted to anyone besides his sons to place incense upon the altar. Among these, some, erring still more, indeed deny that Samuel was of the line of Aaron—that is, they say he was not born a priest—and nonetheless assert that he exercised the priesthood. To these the answer must be given first. For it is worse to deny that Samuel was born a priest and yet to assert that he exercised the priesthood, than to say that he was a priest from among the sons of Aaron. For the former is ignorance, the latter folly. For when those who think him born a priest have learned that he was not from the sons of Aaron, they, though unaware, will hold it manifest that he was not a priest, because it was not permitted to anyone to perform the priesthood except to him who was of the seed of Aaron. For they have it ascertained; for it is manifest that Korah, when he was not of the sons of Aaron and had wished to place incense upon the altar, was swallowed up by a gaping of the earth together with his companions. And King Uzziah, when he was by no means of the seed of Aaron but of the tribe of Judah, and had presumed to perform the priesthood, standing before the altar was struck with leprosy on his forehead and thus expired.

But those who say that Samuel was not born a priest and nonetheless assert that he exercised the priesthood—what they say is foolish enough. And to persuade a fool of what is good is a task of the greatest labor. For by how great a dullness are they led, that, while the sun appears above the earth, they should say that it is night! For although they read—and read in more than one place—that this was decreed by God, that no one should dare to perform the priesthood except Aaron and his sons, with obstinate mind they contend that Samuel was a priest. For they do not understand that, if Samuel was not born a priest and yet performed the priesthood, he is called a presumptuous man, because God established this: that priests should be born, not made. And concerning Samuel I think it is not safe to hold this opinion. For how could it come about that a praiseworthy man, commended by the testimony of God, should do what he knew was not permitted? Of which presumption, moreover, he held for certain that punishment had been inflicted once and again. For neither by the judgment of God could he aspire to this, God whom he knew to be unchangeable; from whom, if perchance he had heard this, he would rather have believed himself to be tempted, knowing that God could in no way rescind his own sentence. For he could sooner believe that this was being done with him under the appearance and name of God, so that he might be deceived by the adversary's side, than that God could change his own judgment.

Finally, when Balaam had been forbidden by God to go to Balak, and afterward had inquired again whether he should go, God, being angered with him, rebuked him by the example of the she-ass, because the ass, seeing the angel who forbade him, was unwilling to complete the journey it had begun. But Balaam, when God forbade him to go, by asking again whether God wished him to go, judged concerning God as concerning a man, who through that which is without foreknowledge is inconstant and changeable. But Balaam is commended by no divine testimony — for he was a soothsayer —, whereas Samuel was a man dear to God and knowing that the decree of His judgments is fixed; how could he have believed that anything ought to happen otherwise than he knew had been established by God?

'But when Eli was dead,' they say, 'and his sons the priests, Samuel began to exercise the priesthood': which neither the reading teaches nor reason allows. For in saying this they suppose that there was then no one who might exercise the priesthood, so that, these three being dead, unless Samuel had offered the people's gifts, the exercise of the priesthood would have ceased; which assertion is hostile to God. For by this God is judged to be improvident; for as though unknowing He establishes that which cannot endure. For to what end did He establish that none other than the sons of Aaron should exercise the priesthood even to the end of the age, that is, until the times of the coming of Christ, if He knew this would fail? But if He does not know — which God forbid! — He was improvident; and therefore it is possible that Samuel was priest when they failed. But if God is provident and foreknowing, that which He established endured; and if that which He established endured, Samuel did not exercise the priesthood, because they were not priests. In the old law God decreed that priests be born, but in the new the Lord commanded that priests be made.

Let them now choose one of two things: let them prove either that Samuel was born a priest or made one. But they agree that he was not born a priest, because they know that he was not of the sons of Aaron. If therefore Samuel was not born a priest, and it is neither read nor proved that he was made one, because God had not decreed that priests be made — it is settled beyond doubt that Samuel was by no means a priest.

But the objectors with closed eyes say: 'If he was not a priest, yet he acted in the priest's stead, since it is read that he offered sacrifice to God!' Who would dare to deny what Scripture proves in writing? For Samuel did offer sacrifice to God, but from this he is not known to have acted in the priest's stead. For he is always said to offer, whose the oblations are, which the priest places upon the altar. And Saul offered — in this same manner, that is, through a priest, just as it is now offered — and David offered and Solomon offered and the rest likewise offered. Did they all act in the priest's stead? For although the priest discharges his own office, yet he is said to offer in whose name the priest acts; for it is imputed to him whose gifts are offered. And he who was not a priest, how could he act in the priest's stead? Can a deacon act in the priest's stead? For a prefect can act in the stead of a prefect, and a praetor in the stead of a praetor, yet a private person cannot act in the stead of any authority: how much more can he not act in the priest's stead, who is not a priest!

For with what intention does he dare to aspire to this, which he knows is not permitted to him? For if a priest is lacking somewhere, a priest of another place can, when asked, come and act in his stead; but a prophet cannot — however holy his life may be — do what he knows has by no means been granted to him. For it is one thing to live well and another to receive the authority of some office. For just as one who is a priest ought not on that account to think his life commended, so also one who is of holy conduct and life will not thereby be entitled to claim the priesthood for himself. For although the priesthood is a good thing, yet it will be an evil for the man to whom it has not been granted and who presumes upon it. For if we consider what is written concerning holy Samuel, we shall see what kind of testimony Scripture gives him, saying: "And it became known," it says, "to all the people, that Samuel is faithful as a prophet of the Lord"; and in the psalm: "Let there be," it says, "Moses and Aaron among his priests, and Samuel among those who call upon his name." Who would not notice, from this distinction, that the persons have been divided by reason of their dignities, so that Moses and Aaron are recognized as having obtained the priestly dignity, while Samuel is held to have stood out as worthy of God among the prophets — who by their prayers called upon God to protect his people, as we read? And the priests are shown to have been so far from lacking, that when the ark had been brought back by the Levite bearers, the men of Beth-shemesh offered sacrifices to God in Samuel's absence. And when Saul had been made king, Ahimaas, the great-grandson of Eli the priest, was the one who carried the ephod.

"But from this," they say, "Samuel seems to have been a priest, because he was clothed with the ephod." As if deacons were not today clothed in dalmatics, just as the bishop is. But we read that David too was clothed with an ephod, and with a double ephod. Samuel, moreover, while still a little boy, was girded with an ephod: could a little boy offer the people's gifts to God? You see, then, that "ephod" is indeed a single word, but does not always signify a single thing. For the priests carried the ephod, they were not clothed with it; but the kings and Samuel the Levite were clothed with the ephod. Sometimes, therefore, "ephod" signifies a garment, and sometimes a kind of little case, which the priests carried for consulting the Lord.

As far as appears, it has been proved that Samuel was not a priest but a prophet. Now we reply to those who, not knowing that Samuel is not of the sons of Aaron the priest, suppose that he was a priest; for it was not lawful that one descended from the line of Aaron should not be a priest. And I want them first to recognize that, if Samuel was a priest, then without doubt Elkanah his father too was a priest. It would also have been fitting that his sons were priests — sons whom, because they were not priests, he appointed as judges for the sons of Israel, just as he himself, Samuel, also was. For thus we read: "that he judged the sons of Israel." But as for Elkanah the father of Samuel, in proof that he was not a priest: "he went up," it says, "from days to days out of his own city Ramathaim to worship and to sacrifice to God almighty of hosts; and there was Eli and his two sons, Hophni and Phinehas, the priests of the Lord."

What is so clear as this: that Elkanah came to offer his gifts before the Lord through the priests at the appointed time, according to what Moses had established, namely that three times a year they should offer their gifts and their tithes, wherever the ark of the Lord and the priests should be — and this indeed although he even had two wives at one time, which is unlawful for priests? For Elkanah was of the Levites, just as the order of the generations is contained in the book of Chronicles. For as yet the Levites did not have an established order of ministry with respect to the priests and the ark of the Lord. For it was David who, in his reign, arranged the courses for the priests and the Levites, so that from twenty years old and upward — [under the law], but from twenty-five years old and upward — they should begin to render their services in the ceremonies of the Lord; so that there should be, from the sons of Aaron, that is, of the line of Phinehas and Ithamar, twenty-four classes of priests, which should perform their courses at fixed times. And the Levites were appointed, some to be the doorkeepers of the tabernacle, and some the bearers of the ark of the Lord, and some to keep watch, and some to be the custodians of the vessels, and some to receive the various offerings. And twenty-four classes were established of singers and harpers and of the other musicians, so that these also, that is, all the Levites, should have their turns of times, because it was necessary for them also to have leisure, so that they might also take care of their own households.

And not only do these things avail for the case stated above — namely, that Samuel was not of the sons of Aaron — but also that which his mother says to the Lord: "If," she says, "you give me a son, I lend him to the Lord all the days of his life." She would not say this if he had been born a priest — for it was fitting that he should serve the altar — but because he was a Levite, and as yet the law had not been laid down for the Levites, but each one acted according to his own will, so that, wandering astray, they presumed unlawful things. For Jonathan, the son of the son of Moses, when he had been assigned among the Levites, presumed to perform the priesthood for the tribe of Dan. And on account of this we read in the book of Judges that "each one," it says, "did what pleased himself, because there was no king in Israel." For this reason Hannah made her vow, saying: "I lend him to the Lord," lest he should go astray with the rest.

And that the question may be more fully examined, let us also treat of that which was said concerning Elkanah, that he came day by day to offer his gifts and his tithes. How did he offer tithes, who possessed nothing? For the Levites did not receive fields, because they sought their sustenance from the tithes which were given by the people. But it can be, and is thus given to be understood, that he could have had the possession of his wife, either inherited or purchased; for they received wives from the other tribes, not only these, but also the rest, so that even the priests took to themselves wives from the other tribes. For Jehoiada the high priest married a wife of the tribe of Judah, the daughter of king Joram.

XLVII. ON THE READING OF ISAIAH THE PROPHET: 'AND SEVEN WOMEN SHALL TAKE HOLD OF ONE MAN, SAYING: WE WILL EAT OUR OWN BREAD AND BE COVERED WITH OUR OWN GARMENTS; ONLY LET YOUR NAME BE INVOKED UPON US. TAKE AWAY OUR REPROACH.'

In sum, the seven women signify the seven churches; for although the Church is one, yet it is called sevenfold, so that one body is composed of a sevenfold number of members. For not only we, but also the celestial beings on high, are members of the Church, whose head is Christ. Therefore, whether the churches be called one or seven, there is no discrepancy. For it is called one because it has one head, which is Christ; but it is called seven because, just as the members are diverse, so also are the spiritual powers. Among these we too are reckoned; the virtues are diverse, and for this reason they are also said to be in need. For they are diverse precisely so that individual members cannot do all things, but that all together may be the body of Christ, since he himself is the head of the body, the Church, from whom the whole body subsists — that is, from whom all things in heaven and on earth have their origin.

In this Church, therefore, which is on earth, mention has been made of all the churches, because, when the mystery of the Creator is preached to this one, a doctrine of this kind is likewise made known to the celestial beings. For when it is imparted to those below, it is necessary that those on high also hear. Whence the Apostle says: To me, the least of all the saints, is given this grace, to evangelize among the Gentiles the incomprehensible riches of Christ, and to enlighten all men, what may be the dispensation of the mystery hidden from the ages in God, who created all things, and that it might be made known to the principalities and powers in the heavens through the Church the manifold wisdom of God. Through this Church, therefore, those on high are taught, because, as he says, truth is sprung out of the earth. For so that mention may be made of those above, here seven churches are named within one people, which seven churches the prophet brings forward as suppliants before the Savior who has become man. For they understood that Christ was born for this purpose: to take away the reproach, first indeed of those living under his law, and then of the rest. For they held in memory that it was written: There shall come out of Sion he who shall deliver and turn away impiety from Jacob.

These seven churches, therefore, laid hold of one man, that is, Christ born, saying: We will eat our own bread and be covered with our own garments; only let thy name be invoked upon us, take away our reproach. What is this that they pray for? For if they use their own bread and are clothed with their own garments — that is, if they both live and are not naked — what do they lack? For if bread signifies that which pertains to life, and clothing that which pertains to devotion to God — because he who is without God is called naked; whence the Apostle says: As many as have been baptized in Christ, you have put on Christ, and again he says: if we be stripped, may we not be found naked —, what is it that they ask, that the reproach be taken away from them, unless it be that this people is signified in the number of the seven churches, which, living under the law, was awaiting Christ promised for the abolishing of sins? Therefore they say: We will eat our own bread — that is, we shall be fed with the words of the law, which hand down one God, because man does not live by bread alone but by every word of God — and we will be covered with our own garments, that is, we are reckoned by the name of our Creator, because each one is said to be clothed with that which he both is and professes.

Finally, senators or officials are understood from their garments as to what they are. But because these things are not sufficient for meriting God's favor, he established this also, that through the sacrament of the knowledge of the one God man might be heir of the kingdom of heaven. For through faith, having been washed from his sins and from the second death — which, by the sentence pronounced in Adam, held men fast among those below — he, now alienated from it with none holding him back, proceeds into the paradise of God the Father, in which the Lord said to the thief that he would be with him. For although the people spoken of above, who were signified in the seven churches, were under the law of God and in devotion from the very origin of the world, they nonetheless had need of purification both from their own and from their forefather's transgression, because "all," he says, "have sinned and lack the glory of God." For this reason the aforementioned churches pray that their reproach may be taken away by the invocation of the name of Christ, because those who have his sign, by which he conquered death, cannot be held by the enemy. And not only these churches pray that the name of Christ be invoked over them, but also the spiritual powers on high dwelling in the heavenly places. For although they are spiritual and heavenly powers, they nonetheless lie under reproach if they should become estranged from their Creator, and they will not even be members of the body, who, not knowing their own head, go astray.

And because it is nothing other than what we have explained, in the following passages the prophet bears witness, saying: "But on that day God will give light in counsel upon the earth," and he added: "for the Lord," he says, "will wash away the filth of the sons and daughters, and will purge the blood from their midst." What could be so evident, that on that day — that is, on which the promise of God was fulfilled and the sacrament of faith was made manifest to men — they were enlightened, so that, purified through the knowledge of the Creator, those who had been guilty of death might become heirs of eternal life? The prophet therefore spoke indiscriminately, so as to signify that all have need of the gift of God, so that, whether sinners or righteous, they might be known to have awaited the mercy of God — sinners on account of their own transgressions, that they might be snatched from the jaws of death, but the righteous, absolved of their forefather's sin, the sentence pronounced in Adam being annulled — by which all were held fast by death — having received liberty, might enter into the kingdom of God, no longer servants, but sons of God.

XLVIII. GOD IS CERTAINLY PERFECTION AND IN NEED OF NOTHING: WHAT THEN WAS THE NEED FOR CHRIST THE SAVIOR TO BE BORN OF GOD, AND FOR GOD TO HAVE A SON THROUGH WHOM HE MIGHT MAKE ALL THINGS?

When God had willed that the things which did not exist should come into being, and knew that this work was by no means worthy of his majesty, first, from himself—since he is a simple nature and incorporeal—he begot a Son, who would differ in nothing from him, so that a result congruent with his greatness might correspond to it. For what more could he do than to beget another self, one who is perfect? This, therefore, is the perfect work, than which nothing could seem more excellent. For all other things are lesser; for by however much Christ is more excellent than all these, by so much the more is the creation of them inferior to his generation. There is also another point. For God, from whom are all things, wishing to found creation, first begot the Word, which he held in mystery within himself—that is, he caused it to exist. This Word he therefore named Son, in order to show that it had come forth from himself and was consubstantial with him, so that the law by which sons are from parents might make this credible, through which he might make manifest the mystery of creation, which lay hidden in him from eternity.

XLVIIII. WHY THE SAVIOR, THOUGH HE WAS BORN HOLY AND WAS CALLED CHRIST THE LORD AT HIS VERY BIRTH, WAS BAPTIZED, SINCE BAPTISM IS FOR THE SAKE OF PURIFICATION AND OF SIN?

It is true and manifest that the Savior had no need of baptism, because Christ was not made but born, as the angel said to the shepherds: behold, today there is born to you a Savior, who is Christ the Lord. Finally, John, knowing his holiness, tried to forbid him from baptism, but the Savior insisted that it ought to be done—not indeed on account of sin, but for the sake of fulfilling righteousness. For it was fitting that he himself should be an example to the future sons of God, he who taught that through baptism men become sons of God; and he who promised that the Holy Spirit would be given to believers ought to demonstrate this visibly in his own self, so that, once this was known, believers might have hope that they invisibly receive the Holy Spirit. For the Savior indeed, since he is born of the Holy Spirit, had a purified body. For the anointing was given to his flesh spiritually in the womb; for the Holy Spirit purified that which, from the Virgin Mary, developed into the body of the Savior. And this is the anointing of the flesh of the Savior's body, wherefore even at birth he was called 'Christ.' For what God used to bestow through the anointing of oil, by the ministry of the prophets, upon those who were anointed as kings, this the Holy Spirit bestowed upon the man Christ, with an expiation added, because the earlier anointed ones received through anointing only the power of rule. But the Savior both received power, born as a man, and was purified, born as he was. For it was unfitting that the Son of God should be born in a body subject to sins.

Therefore, taking up the cause of man and teaching that through regeneration men become sons of God, he had to be baptized, so that he might show this ratified in himself. For what is said is easily held to be proven and is made persuasive, if it is seen to be done by the master. So too, indeed, it was fitting that the signs of miracles should be performed, so that, now appearing as the Son of God through the mystery of regeneration, he might give a remedy to bodily sufferings, that he might be an example to future brothers, because through regeneration each one receives the power of miracle.

L. IF THE SAVIOR WAS BAPTIZED IN ORDER TO BE AN EXAMPLE, WHY, HAVING BEEN CIRCUMCISED, DID HE FORBID THE REST TO BE CIRCUMCISED?

Circumcision is a commandment of the past time, which had to hold authority up until Christ, so that it might run on only as long as until Christ, promised to Abraham, should be born, and thereafter, once the promise was fulfilled, circumcision might cease. For Isaac was promised as a figure of Christ. For God said to him: In your seed shall all the nations be blessed, which is Christ. For the faith which Abraham had received was restored by Christ, so that in the seed of Abraham, which is Christ, all the nations might be blessed, just as it had been promised to Abraham. And so circumcision was a sign of the promised son, that is, of Christ; and once he was born, the sign of the promise had to cease, yet in such a way that the promised one himself, on his coming, should receive the sign of the father, so that it might be known that this was he who had been promised — to justify all the nations through faith in the circumcision of the heart. For just as, to father Abraham, the circumcision of the son being born in the flesh was a bodily seal, so also, for those who are born spiritually, the circumcision of the heart is a spiritual sign; and therefore, more rightly, after Christ it was no longer necessary to be circumcised in the flesh.

LI. HOW IS IT TO BE UNDERSTOOD THAT, WHEN MARY SAID TO THE ANGEL, 'AND WHENCE SHALL I KNOW THIS, SINCE I HAVE NOT KNOWN A MAN?', THE ANGEL GABRIEL ANSWERED: 'THE HOLY SPIRIT SHALL COME UPON YOU AND THE POWER OF THE MOST HIGH SHALL OVERSHADOW YOU.'

To Mary, doubting about the conception, the angel proclaims its possibility, saying: the Holy Spirit shall come upon you, that is: 'do not doubt because you know not a man; for what I said,' he says, 'namely that you shall conceive, the Holy Spirit coming upon you shall bring about, so that you may conceive without a man.' And the power of the Most High, he says, shall overshadow you. The 'power of the Most High' is without doubt Christ; for this pertains to his own person. The Holy Spirit, therefore, coming upon the virgin sanctified her, by his working making a holy body from her, in which the power that is called the Son of God might be born. His overshadowing upon the virgin is this: that from the immensity of the divinity something might be in the womb of the virgin, as much as human nature could contain — which, as if from a splendor, was called the overshadowing of the power of God, and was the power of God and also God: for there is nothing of God which is not called God. For this is a bodily thing, that there should be something in the flesh and yet it cannot be called flesh, such as hairs and bones and the rest.

LII. IF CHRIST WAS BORN OF THE HOLY SPIRIT, THAT IS, BY HIS OPERATION WAS MADE FLESH FROM MARY, WHY WAS IT SAID: 'WISDOM', WHICH INDEED IS CHRIST, 'BUILT HERSELF A HOUSE'?

This question must be understood in a twofold sense. For, first, the house of Christ is the Church, which he built for himself with his own blood. Next, his body too can be called his own house, just as it is also called his temple. For if on account of his dwelling in it he is called the temple of God, it will not be absurd for it to be called a house as well, just as we read in the Law. But if the body was made by the working of the Holy Spirit — the body which we judge can also be called a house — then it is asked why it has been referred to the person of Christ. What the Son does is what the Father does, because there is one power belonging to both. In like manner also what the Holy Spirit does is what the Son of God does, on account of the unity of nature and of will. For whether the Father acts or the Son or the Holy Spirit, it is the Trinity that works; and whatever the three have done is the operation of the one God.

LIII. IF ALL THINGS HAVE BEEN MADE WITH REASON, HOW IS IT THAT THE SAVIOR IS SAID TO HAVE BEEN BORN ON THE EIGHTH DAY BEFORE THE KALENDS OF JANUARY?

No one can be so dull as to deny that God does all things with reason. Therefore Christ, descending from the sacred seats to bestow salvation on the world, in order that he might also teach that the world itself and the seasons were established by him, willed then to be born as man for increasing unto God the diminished state of the human race, at the time when, after a great diminishing, the light — which is the day — begins to receive increase, so that the time of his nativity might accord with the reason of the divine teaching, which began to multiply men out of the shadow of death unto life.

LIIII. IF CHRIST WAS MADE SON TO GOD FROM THE SEED OF DAVID ACCORDING TO THE FLESH — THAT IS, HE IS NOW BORN SON OF GOD IN BOTH RESPECTS, BECAUSE HE WAS BORN HOLY — HOW THEN, AFTER HE WAS BAPTIZED, WAS IT SAID TO HIM BY THE LORD GOD: 'THOU ART MY SON, THIS DAY HAVE I BEGOTTEN THEE'?

Christ is the Son of God from eternity according to the spirit of holiness, but according to the flesh he was born son to God from the seed of David, so that in both respects he is held to be Son to God not by being made, but by being born. But that which he hears at his baptism belongs to the mystery, not to his own case. For this all who are baptized hear. He himself, however, is only being shown forth, so that from this God may appear in the man through mighty works; but the rest are confirmed, because from this they begin to be sons of God, when they receive the Holy Spirit. For although the body of the Lord was born holy, nevertheless the man Christ had not been confirmed by the sacrament of regeneration to be the Son of God, unless he had received the Holy Spirit, according to the decree of the gift of the capacity for rebirth. For the Jews too were called sons of God in devotion, not in the sacrament which now operates, so that, having received remission of sins with the coming upon them of the Holy Spirit, they may be called sons of God. Therefore the Savior both was born the Son of God according to the flesh and was afterward confirmed in the mystery. For that which was born holy of the Holy One could not but be born to God, but, so that the purpose of the mystery might be fulfilled, by the coming upon him of the Spirit he was not diminished, but increased.

LV. WHAT WAS THE CAUSE THAT THE LORD ALLOWED HIMSELF TO BE CRUCIFIED AT THAT TIME, WHEN THE JEWS KEPT THE PASSOVER ON THE EIGHTH DAY BEFORE THE KALENDS OF APRIL?

The Savior accomplished all things in their proper places and times. For, in order to teach that he had rightly founded all things by the nod of the Father, he willed to redeem and reform the world by his passion at that very time when he had also created it — that is, at the equinox, from which the world took its beginning and the day begins to increase over the night. And so, acting within the Roman realm, he had to suffer on none other than the eighth day before the Kalends of April, when the Romans have their equinox. For then, assuredly, this part of the world was first illuminated, and from that point the day began to receive its increase; and therefore also by the Savior's passion it was then led from darkness to light. And so no censure of the Author could seem possible, since he then reformed the fallen creature when he had also made it. Nor indeed could the beginning of creation of a fallen thing be reproached, since its restoration returns to that same point. For he willed the joy of renewal to be on the same day on which had also been the joy of the founding.

LVI. WHY IN MATTHEW THE FATHER OF JOSEPH IS WRITTEN AS JACOB, BUT IN LUKE AS HELI, SO THAT EITHER HE IS UNSKILLFULLY DESCRIBED AS HAVING TWO FATHERS, OR ELSE IT IS NOT KNOWN WHO TRULY IS HIS FATHER?

There is no ambiguity that the father of Joseph was Jacob. For the line, holding its course from David through Solomon, arrives by a straight passage at Jacob, whose son is Joseph; but Heli is the son of Matthias, who from David through Nathan, the son of the same David, holds the order down to the time at which the Savior came. Hence the individual evangelists, having followed out from David the orders of the generations of the several brothers, made as it were a fork: so that Matthew descended from David through Solomon to "Joseph," but Luke ascended from Heli, who lived in the time of the Savior, through the offshoot of Nathan the son of David, and joined the tribe of both Heli and Joseph, showing that both are of one stock — so that, when he associates Heli with Joseph, he shows them not to differ in generation, but to be brothers, and through this that the Savior is the son not only of Joseph, but also of Heli. For by the very same reasoning by which the Savior is called the son of Joseph, by that same he is also the son of Heli and of all the rest who are of the same tribe. Hence it is that the Apostle says: whose are the fathers, and of whom is Christ according to the flesh. For Luke was moved by the divine nod to ascend from Heli through the offshoot of Nathan to David, and through Terah his father to ascend to Shem the son of Noah, and to reach further, beyond the flood, to Seth the son of Adam, who was given in place of Abel, and by the same reasoning to make the Savior the son of Adam by which he was said to be the son of Joseph and of Heli; but transcending beyond Adam, he assigned Christ, before all flesh, to be the Son of God.

But as for that which seems to some — namely, that Heli took the wife of Jacob, in the manner that the Law commanded, that, if anyone had died without children, his brother or a kinsman should take his wife and raise up seed for his brother, and that it was so done that Heli begot Joseph for Jacob, whose wife he had taken, and through this the generation is joined, so that not undeservedly Joseph is said to have Heli as father — this is neither probable nor of any profit for anything.

Now, that which was said above both joins [them] through generation by means of the two brothers, sons of one man, and shows Christ to be the Son of God before every generation. For the evangelist, when he reports, says: and Jesus himself was beginning to be about thirty years old, being the son (as was supposed) of Joseph, who was of Heli — that is, Jesus was reckoned the son of Joseph, and was the son not only of Joseph but also of Heli. Not because he says that Joseph was the son of Heli, but in the same manner in which Joseph was called the father whose son Jesus was, so also he was the son of Heli, because Joseph and Heli were the sons of brothers — that is, of Solomon and Nathan, the sons of David — so that, ascending through David to Abraham and Noah and Seth and to Adam himself, and above Adam, he may teach that Christ is the Son of God. For when he says: who was the son of Seth, who was the son of Adam, who was the son of God, he assuredly calls Christ the son of Adam in the very same way as he was called the son of Joseph. For Mary said to Jesus: Son, why hast thou done so to us? for behold, I and thy father, sorrowing and sad, sought thee as we went about. But above Adam he joins Christ to God the Father, so that he who was called the son of these — that is, from Adam down to Joseph and Heli — should before all these be understood to be the true Son of God, to the confounding of Photinus, who contends that Christ existed only from Mary and not before. For he was called the son of those whose son he was not, while it was denied that he was the son of God, whose son he truly was.

For if — which is improbable and serves no purpose — Joseph be said to be the son of Heli according to what we said above, the evangelist will seem to have said not concerning Christ that he was the Son of God, but concerning Adam. For, by setting the fathers in order under each of the sons individually, he comes to Enos, whose father he says is Seth, and the father of Seth he says is Adam, but the father of Adam he says is God. I do not know what usefulness there is in asserting it thus. But if, in order, as we said, the individual men are called the fathers of Christ — just as he was also called the son of Joseph, because it is said: whose are the fathers, and of whom Christ came according to the flesh — then by that very order he is read to be the son of Seth and the son of Adam, and above all these he is assigned as the Son of God, so that he is said to exist before those very ones whose son he is named.

LVII. HOW IS IT THAT, WHEREAS IT IS WRITTEN IN THE PROPHET MALACHI: 'BEHOLD, I SEND MY ANGEL BEFORE THY FACE, WHO SHALL PREPARE THY WAY', THE EVANGELIST MARK ASSERTS THIS TO BE WRITTEN IN THE PROPHET ISAIAH?

It could not have escaped Mark what he was writing; for he was not without acquaintance with the reading, being one who, imbued from infancy with the divine writings, had been trained in the law, especially since he followed the apostles. But knowing that all things spoken are to be referred to their author, he traced these words back to Isaiah, who had first intimated this sense, saying: the voice of one crying in the wilderness: prepare ye the way of the Lord, make straight the paths of our God. And so, after the words of Malachi, the evangelist immediately subjoined, saying: the voice of one crying in the wilderness, in order to join the words of both prophets, pertaining to one sense, under the person of the earlier prophet.

LVIII. ON WHAT GROUNDS DOES JOHN DENY THAT HE KNEW CHRIST BEFORE THE BAPTISM, WHEN, AS CHRIST COMES TO HIM FOR BAPTISM, HE SAYS: 'I OUGHT TO BE BAPTIZED BY YOU, AND DO YOU COME TO ME?' HOW WAS HE IGNORANT OF THE ONE WHOM HE FORBADE, HUMBLING HIMSELF BEFORE HIM?

John was endowed with such great holiness even from his very cradle that he is believed neither to be deceived nor to deceive, nor to be ignorant of his Lord, who had enlightened him in the womb through the Holy Spirit. And therefore it is true that both when the Spirit descended upon him he recognized him, and that, before he came to the baptism, he was not ignorant of him. For he knew him, but whether he himself was the one who was to administer the gift of God promised to the fathers, he did not know — this is what he professes that he then learned, when he saw the Spirit descend upon him. For thus John says that he was instructed by God: upon whomever, he says, you see the Spirit descending and remaining upon him, he it is who baptizes in the Holy Spirit. The Apostle also attests this: for I say, he says, that Christ was a minister of the circumcision for the truth of God, to confirm the promises of the fathers. This is that in which John did not know the Lord; for although he was not ignorant of his greatness, yet this lay hidden from him, that through him the faith of Abraham was to be fulfilled.

LVIIII. IF BAPTISM IS A HEAVENLY MYSTERY, WHY, WHEN THE LORD SPEAKS TO NICODEMUS, WHO DOUBTS ABOUT BAPTISM, DOES HE SAY: 'IF I HAVE TOLD YOU EARTHLY THINGS AND YOU DO NOT BELIEVE, HOW, IF I TELL YOU HEAVENLY THINGS, WILL YOU BELIEVE?'

He who thinks that baptism consists in a carnal reckoning is not spiritual; nor will he be able to obtain the heavenly gift, who does not believe that he is transformed not through water, but through faith. For the water is seen, but it is the Spirit, who is not seen, that works, so that faith may be in it. For just as water washes away the filth of the body, so the Spirit washes the soul from sins, so that as visible things profit visible things, so the Spirit may profit spiritual things as well. And through this a spiritual reckoning is at work in baptism. For there is more there that is heard than is seen.

Since therefore Nicodemus, being constrained by a carnal reckoning, doubted at this point, the Savior, in order to draw him to faith, made use of a fitting example. So that, to establish an invisible thing, he might give a visible example, one that consists in hearing alone, not in sight; and it is not denied, and yet it is earthly, because it works a thing of the world. Therefore the Lord said to Nicodemus, persuading him: the Spirit breathes where it wills. And you hear its voice, but you do not know whence it comes or whither it goes; so is everyone who is reborn of water and the Holy Spirit — so that, just as the voice of the coming spirit, that is, of the wind, is indeed heard but not seen, as has been said, so also the reckoning of baptism is heard in what is said, yet how it comes about through the Spirit is not seen; nevertheless it is heard when something that is to be is proclaimed by the one who imparts the words, so that what is heard may be believed to come about, and yet the reckoning of the deed is not rendered.

Now, when Nicodemus was not led to faith even by the illustration, he then hears from the Savior: "If," he says, "I have spoken to you of earthly things, and you do not believe, how will you believe, if I speak to you of heavenly things?" He called those words earthly which he had brought forward as an illustration. That is: "If, by the earthly reasoning of the illustration given — the breath of the wind — you do not believe that it can happen, because how it happens is not seen, how could it be that, if I were to give heavenly illustrations, which assuredly you do not know, you would believe?" For a man can be persuaded of what he does not know through that which he does know; as, for example, God says of Christ that he is his true Son, whereas how this is cannot be comprehended; but through that which we do know — namely, how, according to the flesh, sons come to be — we therefore believe that God has said, "Christ is my true Son," so as to signify that he is from his very self. In this way the Savior too wished to commend a matter which can be explained neither in words nor in the mind, through that which is perceptible and is heard by the ears — that is, through the illustration of the spirit, which is the wind, which sensation grasps and the ear hears, but does not know whence it comes; he wished to make believable the working of the Holy Spirit, which cannot be grasped.

But also in the Acts of the Apostles it is read in the same way: "And suddenly," it says, "there came a sound from heaven as of a strong wind coming, and it filled the whole house," and the rest. Behold, plainly by the illustration of the wind he intimates that the Holy Spirit thus came from heaven and sounded, in the manner in which a strong wind sounds over the earth. For Jeremiah too calls the wind a spirit, saying: "The wind blows in every region." And this wind, because it is in this world and is carried about through various places, we do not know whence it comes or whither it goes. But the Holy Spirit comes from heaven, as we read, to enlighten those who believe.

How then does it seem to certain people that the Savior spoke concerning the Holy Spirit: "The Spirit blows where it wills, and you hear its voice, but you do not know whence it comes or whither it goes," when it is established that the Savior spoke these things by way of illustration? For then he added: "So it is," he says, "with everyone who has been reborn of water and the Holy Spirit." What is so plain as that he signified the wind by the spirit? But they think that the wind was not signified for this reason, because he says: "It blows where it wills," as if not every creature, under the law set for it, has been left to its own free choice. For we too go and do what we will, acting under law. Wherefore we too shall render an account — or is it thought possible, and does it not even seem foolish, that, wishing to intimate the working of the Holy Spirit, he should give that very Spirit as the illustration? Therefore I judge the question solved in every respect.

LX. IF "THE LAW AND THE PROPHETS WERE UNTIL JOHN," HOW DOES THE SAVIOR SEND TO THE PRIESTS TO HAVE GIFTS OFFERED FOR THE CLEANSING OF LEPROSY?

This indeed was not a matter of time, but was done for the condemnation of the Jews, so that, since they did not understand that the summit of truth belonging to a better time had been brought about for the profit of their salvation, the truth might bend down to their accusation. For since they regarded the Savior as an enemy of the Law, because for mercy's sake he wished to free them from the burden of the Law—just as had been foretold by the prophet Jeremiah, for he says among other things: and I will give them a new testament, not such as I gave to their fathers—then the Savior, lest he should appear an enemy, as they supposed, by preaching new things, sent the man who had been cleansed of leprosy to the priests to offer gifts for his cleansing, just as Moses had commanded. And that he might testify that this would serve for their accusation, for a testimony, he says, to them, so that in judgment this matter might be a witness against them who called the Savior an enemy of the Law. In this the apostle Paul also followed. For although he preached that it was no longer necessary to be circumcised, he himself circumcised Timothy on account of the offense of the Jews—for he preferred to do a superfluous thing rather than that a tumult should be stirred up by false brethren—which indeed served the error of the Jews. For enough was done for them for the moment, through which they might err forever.

LXI. HOW IS IT THAT, WHEN THE JEWS ACCUSED THE DISCIPLES BECAUSE THEY VIOLATED THE SABBATH BY RUBBING EARS OF GRAIN WITH THEIR HANDS AND EATING THEM, THE SAVIOR BROUGHT FORWARD THE EXAMPLE OF DAVID, THAT HE ATE THE LOAVES WHICH IT WAS NOT LAWFUL FOR HIM TO EAT BUT ONLY FOR THE PRIESTS, THROUGH WHICH THEY DO NOT SEEM TO BE EXCUSED, BUT RATHER TO BE MADE GUILTY TOGETHER WITH DAVID, SEEING THAT DAVID DID NOT EVEN DO THIS ON THE SABBATH?

The Savior wishes to convict the hypocrisy of the Jews by many examples, showing that greater things were committed under the Law and that no one dared to accuse them, so that he might show not only once and again the Sabbath violated under the Law, but also the priestly bread unlawfully taken with the priest himself granting it, and, what is greater, by men of lofty authority. For first Joshua the son of Nun by divine command did not keep the Sabbath, and by this deed the walls of Jericho fell of their own accord. How much it profited not to have kept the Sabbath, but to have kept faith! And the Maccabees, when they had first been cut down, fought on the Sabbath and triumphed over their enemies; and the priests, in order to attend to the Lord's ceremonies, disregarded the Sabbath in the temple. But David, now anointed as king, after he had by the power of God despoiled with arms the slain foreigner, being set upon a journey and suffering the necessity of hunger, received bread from the priest, which it was not lawful for him to eat—but apart from necessity it was not lawful; it was, however, lawful if necessity demanded it—; finally the priest, seeing the necessity, did not refuse, and David, chosen by God, received it without hesitation.

Such also is the case of the sabbath, which is why circumcision on the sabbath is likewise not forbidden. For these things, which are not dangerous, are commanded to be observed in such a way that no harm is done if they are transgressed out of necessity, because they are commanded not for salvation but for reverence; but that which is altogether unlawful is always unlawful and is not softened by any necessity, so that when committed it might do no harm. For that is always unlawful which is prohibited by the laws because it is criminal. But those former things, which we said are sometimes permitted, are such as the lawful fasts, which, when broken out of necessity, do not render people guilty, if there be a cause of the stomach or the weakness of fevers. Knowing these things, therefore, the deceitful Jews accused the disciples, as though they were violating the sabbath, as was said above. But the Savior did not wish to prejudge them concerning the time of the law now fulfilled, lest they should leap forth still further into madness; rather, concerning the past, whence they thought the sabbath was the more to be vindicated, he showed them to be slanderers, and they were confounded not only in the matter of the sabbath, but also in that of the priestly bread, as was shown above.

LXII. HOW IS IT THAT, WHEN THE SONS OF LEAH, WHO WERE OF THE TRIBE OF JUDAH, HAD BEEN SLAIN, RACHEL IS SAID TO BEWAIL HER OWN SONS?

As far as pertains to the history, the sons of Rachel, of the tribe of Benjamin, were long ago, for their own crimes—namely, the deeds of the Sodomites, and the rape which they had committed against the concubine of the Levite man—destroyed and blotted out by the remaining tribes. For which reason she is said to refuse to receive consolation, knowing there is no hope for those who are known to have perished. But the sons of Leah were slain in their earliest years for the Savior's sake, whence he does not wish the lamentation to be ascribed to their case, because they were slain both innocent and for God's sake, by whom without doubt, by way of a reward, they were granted eternal life. Wherefore the lamentation belongs to the sons of Rachel, who were blotted out both in the present and in the future, whereas those others, bewailed carnally, were consoled spiritually; but the sons of Rachel, having lived carnally, shall be consumed by spiritual flames. And for this reason the evangelist testifies that Rachel's lamentation was fulfilled when the sons of Leah were slain, because she then began to bewail her own sons when she saw the sons of her sister slain in such a cause, that they might stand forth as heirs of eternal life. For one to whom something adverse befalls from another's good fortune mourns his own misfortunes the more wretchedly.

LXIII. BY WHAT REASONING DID THE CHALDEAN MAGI UNDERSTAND, THROUGH THE APPEARING OF A STAR, THAT CHRIST, THE KING OF THE JEWS, HAD BEEN BORN, WHEN BY A STAR AS A SIGN A KING IS CUSTOMARILY INDICATED ACCORDING TO THE TIMES?

These Chaldean magi observed the course of the stars not out of malevolence, but out of curiosity about things. For, as we are given to understand, they were following the tradition of Balaam, who, when he had been summoned by Balak to curse the people of God, by divine prompting began to bless. Therefore from his account they had learned that by God's providence one would come from Jacob who would reign. For he — a thing which is not hidden — prophesied, saying: A star shall rise out of Jacob, and the rest. Following, then, this tradition, the magi, seeing the star outside the order of the world, understood that this was the one which Balaam had prophesied would be the sign of the King of the Jews — which indeed came to pass against the enemies of religion. For from that source it received testimony from which it is wont to be disproved; for the astrologers are enemies of the truth.

LXIIII. IN WHAT WAY IS IT PROVED THAT THE SAVIOR ROSE FROM THE DEAD AFTER THREE DAYS AND NIGHTS?

In this matter, if you look for the number according to a strict sequence of days and nights, you will not arrive at a satisfactory understanding, because Moses too fasted forty days and forty nights, and yet the full number is not found. For when he ascended during a day and descended during a day, he assuredly did not complete the whole number; but because, where there is a day, the night also is reckoned, and where there is a night, the day also is reckoned, so that from a part to the whole they are called forty days and forty nights. So it is also with what the Savior said, so that, because there are three nights, three days too are reckoned. For there is a night — lest perhaps it seem novel or contrary to reason — since night depends on day. For that it was instituted before the making of the light, from which it was called "day," rather than before the evening, which night follows, is by no means doubted.

That the Lord's passion is affirmed to take its beginning from night is not absurd; for just as light, that is, day, is the image of life, so night is the likeness of death, that is, darkness, as is plainly shown in the Scriptures, namely: sons of light and, on the contrary: of darkness. Nor is it any wonder if, although everywhere day is set before night and light before darkness, here alone the things that are subsequent are placed before the things that are prior, or that in such a matter the order of things is confused and changed, so that the night, as the standard-bearer of death, seems to be more than the day — for indeed the beginning is taken from night — since one could not otherwise steal in upon the prince of darkness except through night, and so that to some extent the Lord of light, that is, of eternal life, might be for a time made subject to the prince of darkness or of death, insofar as he might free from death both those of the past and those to come afterward. For death would not have been utterly emptied, nor the gloom of darkness ever dispersed, if it had not seen the Lord. For with so great a light stealing in, the secret place of death, in which it held dominion, vanished; nor can it be utterly conquered except by one who is seized either through his own or in his own. Rightly, therefore, in such a business does the night alone hold the primacy, in such a way that it should lose its power. And so that the Jews, not believing, might remain in perpetual night, and that the night, not the day, might become the author of so great a crime — nay rather of sacrilege — the day is made subject to the preceding night against the sequence of things, just as God and Lord of all things was made subject to the prince of wicked death, that he might release all from the snares of death.

Now if perchance this still seems contrary to someone, let him attend carefully, lest he begin to judge too harshly the fact that God, clothing himself in the person of a servant — I will not say of a man — gave himself over to death. Why then do you here seek order, where you see that all things are contrary? For what is the light which was in the darkness, and the darkness did not comprehend it, by which it was seized? For he who knows that he is being seized for this purpose, that he be struck down, counts that time unto death. There is also the following day, on which he was heard and crucified; there is also the night that falls upon the Sabbath; there is also the Sabbath itself; there is also the evening after the Sabbath — this is what was commanded to the Jews by Moses in a figure, that they should enter into the Sabbath in the evening —, on which the Lord rose again, which embraces the Lord's Day, because a night is not reckoned without a day nor a day without a night. By this reckoning, after three days and three nights the Lord rose again.

LXV. IF THE EVANGELISTS SPOKE WITH ONE MOUTH AND ONE REASONING, HOW DID IT COME ABOUT THAT, WHILE THREE SAY — THAT IS, MATTHEW, LUKE, AND JOHN — THAT THE LORD WAS CRUCIFIED AT THE SIXTH HOUR, MARK ON THE CONTRARY SAYS THAT THE SAVIOR WAS CRUCIFIED AT THE THIRD HOUR?

It is not good to wrap up truths in obscurities. For the three evangelists had one meaning, but Mark wished to make known a matter which had been passed over by them, knowing it to be necessary. For he could not be deceived, who, following the examples of the authors, learned with great devotion and diligence the things which he wrote, and was not without the Holy Spirit. What therefore he wished to show from this ought to be resolved. It must therefore be considered that the Savior was crucified not by Pilate, but by the Jews. Now as far as pertained to the Roman laws, they pronounced the Savior innocent. For Pilate said to the Jews: I find no cause in him; and when they said, Crucify him, he replied: Why, what evil has he done? Finally, persisting and wishing to lead him out of their hands, he suffered slander when they said: If you release this man, you are not Caesar's friend. For everyone who makes himself a king contradicts Caesar. Thus it came about that he handed him over to their judgment. Therefore it was not Pilate who gave the sentence, but the Jews.

Finally, they were forewarned, he says, by the chief priests, that they should say: Let him be crucified. He wishes this sentence to be understood as given at the third hour, in which, persisting with unceasing shouts, yet with an interval of about three hours, during which there was a going and returning from Herod, they crucified the Savior. For everyone who is condemned is from then already counted as dead, from the moment he receives the sentence. Mark therefore made manifest that the Savior was not crucified by the sentence of the judge. For it is difficult to prove him innocent who is punished by the sentence of a judge. He therefore allowed himself to be in discord in a word, so that he might teach that what was completed at the sixth hour had been begun at the third hour, not by the laws, but by the persisting malevolence of the Jews.

LXVI. THE EVANGELIST MARK SAYS THAT THE DEMONS KNEW AND CONFESSED JESUS, BUT THE APOSTLE, ON THE CONTRARY, DENIES THAT THE PRINCES AND POWERS OF THIS WORLD KNEW THE DIVINITY OF THE LORD JESUS. FOR MARK SAYS, AMONG OTHER THINGS: 'FOR THEY KNEW HIM TO BE'; BUT THE APOSTLE SAYS: 'WHOM NONE OF THE PRINCES OF THIS WORLD KNEW; FOR IF THEY HAD KNOWN, THEY WOULD NEVER HAVE CRUCIFIED THE LORD OF MAJESTY.' IF THE DEMONS KNEW, HOW DID THE PRINCES NOT KNOW?

To some it seems that 'the princes of this world' signified the leaders of the Jews, as though in accord with what the apostle Peter said: for you know, brethren, he says, that through ignorance you did this evil, as also did your princes. Therefore they were princes of the Jews, yet not of this world. For he says 'your princes', not of the world, seeing that they said they had Caesar as king, under whose power they had been brought. But these princes are those whom the apostle signified in another place, saying: our struggle is not against flesh and blood, but against principalities and powers, against the rulers of these darknesses of this world. Rightly, therefore, is the question raised. For if these did not know Jesus, how could it come about that the demons recognized him?

But it is one thing that he says the demons knew in Christ, and another that he denies the princes of this world recognized. For the demons indeed knew him to be the very one who had been promised through the law. For they saw in him all the signs which the prophets had foretold would come, and that from the seed of David, from a virgin, the redeemer of Israel would come: but the mystery of his divinity they did not know, just as neither did their princes. Finally, the devil asks the savior — though craftily — saying: if you are the son of God, and the rest. For seeing at one time his divine power, at another the weakness of the man, being in doubt as to what was true, he was tormented. Therefore the scriptures agree according to those things which have been revealed. For it is impossible that men of one spirit should disagree.

LXVII. WHAT IS THE MEANING OF THE SAVIOR'S SAYING WHEN PLACED ON THE CROSS: 'FATHER, FORGIVE THEM; FOR THEY KNOW NOT WHAT THEY DO'? IF THEY DO NOT KNOW, WHAT IS IT THAT IS FORGIVEN, ESPECIALLY SINCE KING ABIMELECH SAYS TO GOD: 'WILT THOU DESTROY AN IGNORANT NATION?'

Not everyone who is ignorant is free from punishment. For that man can be excused from punishment who has found no one from whom he might learn; but for these he asks that this be forgiven, because, having someone from whom they might learn, they gave no heed. Ignorance of this kind is not permitted: therefore they will receive pardon if they are converted.

LXVIII. THE LORD ASSUREDLY TAUGHT THAT WE SHOULD PRAY FOR OUR ENEMIES: HOW IS IT THAT, ON THE CONTRARY, THE SOULS OF THE SLAIN ASK TO AVENGE THEMSELVES, DEMANDING VENGEANCE FROM GOD?

Thus the souls of the slain cry out, demanding that they be avenged, just as the blood of Abel cried out from the earth. They are, therefore, causes which are said to cry out, even though they cannot speak. For what else does the blood that has been shed demand than that it be avenged, crying out not with a voice, but by reason? For a work too is said to praise its maker through this very fact, that it delights the one who beholds it. For the saints are not so impatient as to press for something to be done which they know will come to pass at a predetermined time, which can neither be anticipated nor deferred. But by saying this he wished to show that God will avenge the blood of his saints, lest — because he now seems so patient — the impious war that is waged against the saints be thought to go unpunished; so that he might both strike terror into those who persecute God's servants and encourage those who suffer for his sake. For the soul of the one who suffers is relieved when it hears that it will be avenged by one who is powerful. For he displays it openly, if he hears that his death is displeasing to the judge; for then he holds it for certain that he is innocent. And God indeed is merciful and patient, but with measure. For he waits that the impious may believe and that sinners may amend themselves; but if not, they shall be punished, because they have despised God's long patience.

He showed an example of this matter even in the time when mercy was proclaimed, lest he should seem not patient, but insensible, and one whom neither anyone's grief nor piety would seem to move. Hence it is that he says through the prophet: I have held my peace; shall I always hold my peace? And the Lord says: Shall not God, he says, take vengeance for his servants who cry to him day and night? Thus indeed they cry out, just as we said above. If, therefore, any Christian avenges for a time, not harshly nor with blood, he does not sin; yet he will do better if he leaves it to God the judge.

LXVIIII. IF THE LAW HAS ALREADY CEASED WITH JOHN OR THE SAVIOR PREACHING, HOW DOES THE SAVIOR SAY: 'I HAVE NOT COME TO ABOLISH THE LAW OR THE PROPHETS, BUT TO FULFILL'? FOR IF IT HAS BEEN PROHIBITED, HOW HAS IT NOT BEEN ABOLISHED, SINCE IT HAS LOST THE AUTHORITY OF ACTING?

All the things that were said concerning Christ have been fulfilled. And the Lord himself thus fulfilled the law and the prophets, when he did all the things that were written concerning himself and dissolved nothing, but confirmed it. For the law and the prophets were until him. For the prophets spoke concerning him; therefore the things that were said by them concerning him cannot be extended beyond him, nor could any prophets of this kind be found after him, because they have nothing about which to speak, and he of whom they were speaking has already come. For they embraced all things in their volumes, and they revealed both the incarnation and the manner of life and the passion and the resurrection and the manifestation of the divinity and his future judgment, and through this the prophets ceased once the work of the dispensation was fulfilled.

But the Law ceased in a twofold manner, and indeed not wholly; for even that which ceased will be able to remain, if the condition be kept. For one part ceased in its sentence, another in the Law itself. When John preached the baptism of repentance for the remission of sins, the sentence of the Law ceased, which held sinners guilty; there ceased also the burdens of the Law, which had been given, because of the hardness of the Jewish heart, in the matter of foods, new moons, and weasels. For when mercy came, vengeance ceased. But the burdens of the Law ceased forever, whereas the sentence ceases and is abolished for those who remain in the benefit they have obtained. Yet for those who return to the old man the authority of the Law is chafed open again, because, unmindful of the benefits, they return under the sentence of the Law.

But circumcision and the sabbath held good up until that time in which the commandment of the new law should be preached. For they were given in such a way that, when the law of faith came, they would cease. Whence the apostle says: Christ is the end of the Law. For Daniel too signifies this, when he prophesies concerning the coming of the Lord and the times of the weeks, that both the chrism and the judgment and the sacrifice and the city itself would cease. For, the spiritual law having come, it was necessary that the carnal things should cease. For then God was served by a part of the body, now by a part of the soul; formerly visibly, now invisibly; then in the flesh, now in the mind, because God, who is assuredly spirit, must be served in spirit. Therefore the Law has not been abrogated because it ceased, but was succeeded when its time was fulfilled. For neither its administration nor its judgment is blamed if indulgence is given to sinners, since rather from this it is proved to have been rightly and justly given, because those over whom it ruled are not denied to have been sinners: because, he says, the Law is not laid down for the just.

Therefore, it is not to be thought that, because mercy is to be preferred, justice ought to be condemned—justice, without reverence for which mercy itself would bear no fruit. For unless they keep this justice after mercy has been received, forgiveness will profit them nothing. For the Law said: You shall not make for yourself an idol, nor worship the things that are above in heaven and the things that are below on earth, and: You shall not swear falsely, and: Honor your father and mother, and: You shall not kill, nor commit fornication, nor commit theft, you shall not give false testimony, nor covet anything of your neighbor's. Are these to be said to have ceased? Far from it. For without these, who could be judged fit even in this life? And accordingly the other things have ceased which we mentioned above—new moons, sabbaths, the law of foods, sacrifices, circumcision, and the rest. Hence it is that the Apostle says, among other things: Rulers are not a terror to good work, but to evil. Do you wish, then, not to fear the power? Do good, and you shall have praise from it. These things, when kept, make men good, yet not perfect. Whence the Savior says: Unless your justice abound more than that of the scribes and Pharisees, you shall not enter into the kingdom of heaven. For by adding to these the more excellent things, the Savior did not by any means abolish the Law, but fulfilled it. For the meaning of the Law pertains to the salvation of man, as for instance: an eye for an eye, a tooth for a tooth, so that a man, fearing lest he suffer what another was forbidden to do, might restrain himself from wickedness. But the Savior, adding a higher justice to this meaning, says: But I say to you, not to resist evil; but if anyone strike you on your right cheek, offer him the left also, so that, while he does not return like for like to the evil man, he may be perfect. For to return like for like is just, but not full; but if he overlook the injury, the justice is full and abounding. For to repay is a rejoicing for a time; but to remit provides gladness for the future.

Thus, then, the Savior fulfilled the Law, since those whom it taught justice, he made more just—which it could not do—wherefore the joy of the Law is that its disciples were made more skilled. He would plainly have destroyed the Law, if he had taught that one may sin with impunity. But moreover he suspended the sentence, so that he who does evil might have space for repenting; if not, the sentence returns upon him heaped up, because he did not recognize that he was granted this reprieve in order that he might amend himself.

LXX. THE LORD CERTAINLY COMMANDED US TO BECOME ENEMIES TO THE DEVIL; HOW THEN IS IT THAT IN THE GOSPEL HE SAYS: 'BE QUICKLY AGREEING WITH YOUR ADVERSARY'? WHO IS MAN'S ADVERSARY BUT THE DEVIL?

There is no doubt that the devil is the enemy of man, especially of the faithful; for he sharpens his more violent weapons against the servants of God. Just as, therefore, this one is the enemy of the good, so also the law is opposed to the wicked. For who does not oppose one who despises him? The Lord therefore addresses the sinner, that he may consent to the commandments — which condemn him as disobedient — that he may subject himself to their will and, from an enemy, become a friend, since the despiser of the law is also its enemy; for he resists its will. And therefore the Lord exhorts the sinner, that by acting well he may reconcile the law to himself, lest on the day of judgment it accuse him before the judge and, condemned, he pay the penalties for the law he has scorned. For to everyone who wishes to act wickedly the Lord's discipline seems an enemy; and unless he consents to it, he will be cast into the Gehenna prepared for the devil, who is truly the enemy of the human race.

LXXI. JACOB WAS CALLED THE MAN WHO SEES GOD, AND MOSES SAW GOD FACE TO FACE, AND LIKEWISE ISAIAH: 'I HAVE SEEN,' HE SAYS, 'THE GOD OF SABAOTH WITH MY OWN EYES': BUT ON THE CONTRARY JOHN THE EVANGELIST: 'GOD,' HE SAYS, 'NO ONE HAS EVER SEEN.' THIS, AS IT SEEMS, IS CONTRADICTORY.

As far as pertains to the truth of the faith, no one has ever seen God at all, neither the Father nor the Son. For what is said to be "seen" is referred to the understanding; for he was seen as if in an image. Just as we, when we do not know emperors, see them in a likeness, not in reality, so also God was seen, so that he who appeared might be understood to be God, through reasoning, not through substance, since in his own nature God cannot be seen. And that we may more truly unfold the hidden things of the proposed question, let us strive to explain the meaning of the evangelist. For John wished to bring forth something hidden, which he knew pertained to saving doctrine. Therefore he says: God no one has ever seen, except the only-begotten Son, who is in the bosom of the Father. He himself has declared him.

Let us consider the meaning of the evangelist. For in order to show that it is true that no one has ever seen God, he teaches that the Son has declared this — the Son, who indeed cannot possibly be deceived, since he is in the bosom of the Father. But what is the bosom of the Father, if not the affection in the love of the true Father toward the Son through the unity of nature? For which reason no one has seen God, except the only Son. This John the apostle heard the Son of God saying, among other things: not that anyone has seen the Father, except him who is from God; he has seen the Father. Therefore, that it might avail for the condemnation of the Jews, who were unwilling to hear or to believe that Christ is the Son of God, the evangelist showed that this is the Christ who had appeared to the fathers as God; but that he who is the Father is never seen except by the Son. For when he denies that God the Father was seen and professes that God appeared to the fathers, the Son of God wishes to make himself manifest, since he himself was always seen as God by the fathers. Hence it is that among other things he says to the Jews concerning the Father: neither have you ever heard his voice nor seen his form. Behold, it is not contradictory for God to be both seen and unseen.

LXXII. (LXXVI). IN THE GOSPEL JOHN SAYS: 'THE LAW WAS GIVEN THROUGH MOSES, BUT GRACE AND TRUTH WERE MADE THROUGH JESUS CHRIST': THEREFORE BEFORE IT DID NOT EXIST. HOW THEN CAN THE LAW BE SAID TO HAVE BEEN GIVEN BY GOD, IF THE TRUTH WAS NOT IN IT?

This is not to be passed over so casually, but it must be considered what 'the law was given through Moses' means. For the law given through Moses has manifest precepts, but he also wrote a history, which itself too is called law. And let us see what in his precepts will not be true. Perhaps that which it says: you shall not kill, you shall not commit fornication, you shall not steal; such are these and the rest. For as to his history, that before the coming of Christ it was not truth, this is manifest. For those things which were under a veil, what they signified, was uncertain. But when through Christ it is made manifest whose person it is that says in Genesis: let us make, and who it is that makes, and who it was that was seen in the bush or among the patriarchs, and who it was that worked in the rock, which gave waters in the desert — because the rock, he says, was Christ — thus truth is made through Christ. When those things which lay hidden or came into doubt, what they signified, was shown by Christ. For among other things the Lord says: Moses wrote of me. This before lay hidden; for there was error. For he was thought to be God the Father who was the Son, and he who was reckoned an angel was recognized to be the Son of God. And a promise had been made to Abraham, which, as long as it was not paid back, was in ambiguity. But when it was paid back at the coming of Christ, truth was made, when both that which was promised was rendered and it began to be known what had been promised. For the good faith of the one promising is then proved true, when he discharges the promise.

LXXIII. (LXXVII). WHAT IS IT THAT, AMONG OTHER THINGS, THE EVANGELIST MARK SAYS ABOUT CHRIST: 'ENTERING', HE SAYS, 'INTO A HOUSE HE WISHED NO ONE TO KNOW, AND HE COULD NOT BE HIDDEN'? IF THEREFORE HE WISHED AND COULD NOT, HIS WILL SEEMS TO BE WEAKENED.

It is altogether impossible that the Savior's will should not be fulfilled, nor can he will what he knows ought not to be done; therefore that which was done, this he must be said to have willed. For his will is never outside his nature. As therefore his nature does not fall under reproach, neither does his will. For that which was set forth is read to have been done in the borders of Tyre. Then he entered into a house and wished no one to know. Now it is asked in what way or why he wished no one to know. For it must be observed that this was done in the borders of the Gentiles, for whom the time of preaching was not yet. Finally, sending his disciples, he charged them, saying: go not into the way of the Gentiles, and enter not into the city of the Samaritans, but go rather to the sheep which have perished of the house of Israel.

For this reason he did not wish to be disclosed as being in the house; yet he did not refuse to be sought out, but willingly accepted it. For although it was not the time for preaching to the Gentiles, still it would have been a mark of envy not to receive those who came of their own accord to the faith. Thus it came about that the Savior, while he was not disclosed by his disciples, was nevertheless disclosed by others who had seen him entering the house, and it began to be known that he was in the house, so that those who wished to obtain benefits might come in to him. By his own, then, he did not wish to be proclaimed as being in the house. For he did wish to be sought out, and so it was done. For it was not hidden, once it was pointed out by others that he was in the house. And so the Canaanite woman, hearing about him, came in to him, begging that he would drive out the demon from her daughter—who, unless she had first subjected herself to the God of the Jews, would not have obtained the benefit. The will of the Savior, therefore, was fulfilled in accordance with what we have explained; for those things which the evangelist, aiming at brevity through compression, has drawn together, we, examining them, find what lay hidden.

LXXIIII. (LXXVIII). IT IS READ IN THE GOSPEL OF JOHN. THAT WHEN THE SAVIOR HAD DENIED THAT HE WOULD GO UP TO THE FEAST DAY, HE WENT UP. THIS SEEMS TO BE THE MARK OF AN INCONSTANT PERSON.

You always conceal the sense by an abbreviated statement. For this which you call into question happened at the time when, being situated in Galilee on account of the tumult of the Jews, he was being urged by his brothers—who did not yet believe in him—to go up into Judea, because the feast day of the Jews was going to be at hand, so that he might suffer sedition. But he himself answered them, saying: Go you up to the feast day, for the world does not hate you; but me it hates, because I convict its works. I do not go up to this feast day, because my time is not yet fulfilled. Then his brothers went up to the feast day, but he himself remained in Galilee. Afterward, however, he too went up to the feast day.

What seems contrary, when he did not go up at the time when he denied it, but went up afterward, and went up not as to a feast day, but as to a conflict? For they all went up joyfully, as if to enjoy the delights of the feast day. It is certain, therefore, that he did not go up to the feast day. But that was the Savior's feast day, on which by his passion he redeemed the world. And so he says: Now is the Son of Man glorified, and God is glorified in him. This is his feast day, on which he conquered death.

LXXV. (LXXIX). IF WE LIVE BY OUR OWN CHOICE, WHY DID THE SAVIOR SAY: 'NO ONE COMES,' HE SAYS, 'TO ME, UNLESS THE FATHER WHO SENT ME HAS DRAWN HIM,' AND THE APOSTLE, AGREEING WITH THESE: 'IT IS NOT OF HIM THAT WILLS,' HE SAYS, 'NOR OF HIM THAT RUNS, BUT OF GOD THAT SHOWS MERCY,' AND: 'ON WHOM HE WILLS HE HAS MERCY, AND WHOM HE WILLS HE HARDENS'? IN WHAT WAY IS THE CHOICE OF THE WILL FREE, WHEN BY ANOTHER'S BIDDING IT IS LED EITHER TO GOOD OR TO EVIL?

The matter stands otherwise than it has been set forth; for the meaning of this question is not that which you allege. For in no way can the case of free will be disturbed by these words, because if you thoroughly attend to the sense of what is said, you will know that from here the doctrine of free will is rather confirmed. For these things were uttered against the malevolent Jews. For when, out of the deceit of a pretense arising from envy, they asserted that Joseph was the Savior's own father and his sons the Savior's brothers, lest he should be believed to be the Son of God, then the Savior said: No one comes to me, unless the Father who sent me has drawn him. But in what way did the Father draw men to the Son, except through the works which he did through him? For thus he said: The Father, remaining in me, himself works — so that these works might draw them to faith in Christ. For the mighty deeds which the Savior did, these themselves persuaded men that God was the Father of Christ, so that whoever said that he had another father was not drawn by God to Christ. Therefore, then, God was working through Christ, so that credit might be lent to his words, by which he called himself the Son of God.

This is the drawing — not violence, but the testimony of God in Christ; and whoever has believed this is said to be drawn by him to Christ. For no one believes the Savior except him who calls God his own Father.
